The Permissibility of Seeing Allah in the Afterlife
Sanusi affirms the permissibility of seeing Allah with physical sight, befitting His majesty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the beatific vision and the three proofs Sanusi offers for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah in the afterlife is permissible but without spatial direction or facing.

This lesson explores Sanusi's affirmation that believers may see Allah in the afterlife with their physical sight, a sight that befits His majesty without any anthropomorphism. Sanusi grounds this in revelation, prophetic precedent, and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the claim Sanusi makes.
Notice the concise style—Sanusi states the ruling, its conditions, and then three proofs.
2
Identify the three proofs
The passage gives three separate proofs: a Qur'anic verse (al-Qiyama 23), the request of Prophet Moses, and the consensus of the early Muslims (Salaf). Identify each one and see how they support permissibility.
3
Understand the negation of direction and facing
Sanusi explicitly says the vision is not in a direction (jiha) nor facing (muqābala). Reflect on why this is important to preserve tanzih (divine transcendence).
This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih).
4
Connect to broader Ash'ari theology
Consider how this passage fits into the broader Ash'ari approach: affirming what revelation affirms while negating any creaturely limitations from Allah.
This is a key example of the principle of ithbāt (affirmation) with tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في جواز رؤيتِهِ جل وعزَّ
ويجوز في حقه تعالى أن يُرى بالأبصار على ما يليقُ بهِ جل وعلا ، لا في جهةٍ ولا مقابلةٍ ؛ لقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِلَى رَبِّهَا ناظِرَةٌ [القيامة : ۲۳] ، ولسؤال موسى عليهِ السلامُ لها ؛ إِذْ لو كانَتْ مستحيلةً ما جهل أمرها ، ولإجماع السلف الصالح
Chapter. On the permissibility of seeing Him, may He be glorified and exalted. And it is permissible in His right, exalted is He, to be seen with [physical] sights in a manner befitting Him, may He be glorified and exalted, not in a direction nor facing; because of His statement, exalted: 'Faces that day are looking at their Lord' [al-Qiyama 23], and because of the request of Moses, peace be upon him, to see Him; since if it were impossible, he would not have been ignorant of its matter, and because of the consensus of the righteous predecessors.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of the Ash'ari position on the beatific vision (ru'yat Allah). It states that it is permissible (yajūz) for Allah to be seen with physical sight (absār) in a manner befitting His majesty, without spatial direction (jiha) or facing (muqābala). Three proofs are given: first, the Qur'anic verse 'Faces that day are looking at their Lord' (al-Qiyama 75:23); second, the fact that Prophet Moses asked Allah to see Him (if it were impossible, Moses would not have asked); third, the consensus (ijmā') of the early Muslims (salaf). The passage emphasizes that sight of Allah does not imply any spatial or anthropomorphic attributes—it is a sight that befits His transcendence.

Key Terms
رؤية
أبصار
جهة
مقابلة
سلف صالح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah is seen, He must be in a direction or have a physical form like created beings.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly negates direction (jiha) and facing (muqābala), affirming that the vision is in a manner that befits Allah's transcendence, without any creaturely attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is it permissible for Allah to be seen?
A) Because it is logically necessary.
B) Because of revelation, the request of Moses, and consensus.
C) Because He is physical.
D) Because humans have physical eyes.

Key Takeaway
The beatific vision is permissible, but it is without direction or facing, as supported by the Qur'an, the example of Moses, and the consensus of the early Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Moses, a great prophet, asked to see Allah. Do you long for that vision as he did, or have you become content with just knowing about Him? What would change in your daily worship if you truly hoped to see Him?
?
If seeing Allah is possible but beyond direction and facing, how does that shape your understanding of His nearness? Are you avoiding imagining Allah in human terms, or do you still catch yourself thinking of Him as limited?
?
The righteous predecessors agreed on this truth. What does that unity mean for you when you encounter doubts about unseen realities? Will you trust their consensus, or let your own reasoning lead you astray?

Defending the Vision of Allah with Hadith and Quran
Sanusi defends vision of Allah using hadith and refutes two Quranic objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends the vision of Allah in the afterlife using hadith and responds to two Quranic objections through careful interpretation.

Core Idea
Even Quranic verses that seem to deny seeing Allah admit interpretations that uphold the possibility.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a scriptural defense for the vision of Allah (ru'yah) in the afterlife. He begins by citing the practice of the early Muslims and the hadith 'You will see your Lord,' noting that abundant textual evidence yields certainty. He then tackles two Quranic verses often cited against the vision: 'Vision comprehends Him not' and 'You will not see Me.' Through precise linguistic and logical analysis, he shows these verses do not contradict the belief. This lesson unpacks his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Note how Sanusi structures his defense: first positive evidence, then refutation of two objections.
The Arabic is from Sanusi's text; the translation is literal.
2
Identify the two objections
Find where Sanusi mentions each Quranic verse: 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' and 'Lan tarani'. Observe his response to each.
3
Understand the key distinction between idrak and ru'yah
Grasp why comprehension (idrak) is narrower than vision. Sanusi argues that idrak implies encompassment, which is negated, but vision itself is not.
This is the core of the first response.
4
Consider the temporal qualification
Notice how Sanusi limits 'Lan tarani' to this world using the principle of correspondence in answers and logical negation of time-bound propositions.
The logical principle supports that the negation is specific to the time of Musa's request.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
See how Sanusi combines positive textual evidence (hadith) with refutation of objections to establish certainty.
This shows the method of defending beliefs using both proof and response to doubts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل ظهورِ البدع على ابتهالهم إلى الله تعالى وطلبهم النظر إلى وجهه الكريم ، ولحديثِ : « سَتَرَوْنَ رَبَّكُمْ » ونحوِهِ ممَّا ورد ، والظواهر إذا كثُرَتْ في شيء أفادَتِ القطع به . ولا يعارضها قوله تعالى : ( لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ) الأنعام : ۱۰۳] لأنَّ الإدراك أخص ؛ لإشعاره بالإحاطة ، ولا شك أنَّها منفية مطلقاً . سلَّمنا أنَّهُ الرؤيةُ ، لكن المراد في الدنيا ، أو هو مِنْ بابِ الكل لا الكلية . ولا قوله جل وعزّ : ﴿ لَن تَركني ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٣] لأنَّ المراد في الدنيا ؛ إذْ هو المسؤول لموسى عليه السلام ، والأصل في الجواب المطابقة ، ولهذا قالَ : لَن تَرَينِي ولم يقل : لنْ أُرى ، أو : لن تمكن رؤيتي ، وقد يُتَأَنَّسُ لذلكَ بما تقرَّرَ في المنطقِ : أَنَّ نقيض الوقتيّةِ يُؤخَذُ فِيهِ وقتها المعيَّنُ .
Before the appearance of innovations, they pleaded to Allah Almighty and asked to look at His noble face, and because of the hadith: 'You will see your Lord' and similar narrations. And the apparent meanings (zawahir) when they abound in something yield certainty. And it is not contradicted by His saying: 'Vision comprehends Him not' (al-An'am 6:103) because comprehension (idrak) is more specific, as it indicates encompassment, and there is no doubt that it is negated absolutely. We grant that it is vision, but the intended meaning is in this world, or it is from the type of 'all' not 'totality.' And not His saying, may He be glorified: 'You will not see Me' (al-A'raf 7:143) because the intended meaning is in this world, as it was asked by Musa (peace be upon him), and the principle in answering is correspondence, and therefore He said 'You will not see Me' and did not say 'I will not be seen' or 'My vision will not be possible.' And one may seek support for that by what is established in logic: that the negation of a time-bound proposition takes its specific time.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural defense of the vision of Allah (ru'yah) in the afterlife. The author begins by stating that before the appearance of innovations, the early Muslims used to beseech Allah to see His noble face, and they relied on the hadith 'You will see your Lord' and similar reports. When such textual evidences (zawahir) are abundant, they yield certainty. The author then addresses two Quranic objections. First, the verse 'Vision comprehends Him not' (La tudrikuhu al-absar) is not a contradiction because 'idrak' (comprehension) is more specific than vision; it implies encompassing, and its negation is absolute, so it does not negate vision itself. Even if we grant that 'idrak' means vision here, the negation applies to this world only, or it is a negation of the category of vision as a whole (kul) not each individual instance (kulliyya). Second, the verse 'You will not see Me' (Lan tarani) addressed to Musa is specific to this world, as the request was for a worldly vision. The answer matched the question; Allah said 'You will not see Me' rather than 'I will not be seen,' which would negate vision absolutely. This is supported by the logical principle that the negation of a time-bound proposition takes its specific time.

Key Terms
الرؤية
الإدراك
الظواهر
البدع
الوقتيّة
نقيض الوقتيّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Quranic verses 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' and 'Lan tarani' absolutely negate any possibility of seeing Allah.
Correction: Sanusi shows that these verses either negate comprehension (not vision) or are limited to this world, so they do not contradict the vision of Allah in the afterlife.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' not contradict the vision of Allah in the afterlife?
A) Because 'idrak' is more specific than vision, implying encompassment, and its negation is absolute.
B) Because the verse is abrogated by the hadith.
C) Because the verse refers only to the Prophet's vision.
D) Because 'absar' means physical eyes, not spiritual vision.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi shows that abundant scriptural evidence supports the vision of Allah, and the seemingly contrary Quranic verses are either about comprehension (not vision) or limited to this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about standing before Allah and seeing Him with your own eyes, does your heart long for that moment with certainty? Or do you find yourself or others doubting it because of the verses you've heard? What in this lesson exposes the weakness of those doubts, and what will you do to strengthen your conviction?
?
You have read that the early Muslims used to plead to see Allah's face before innovations appeared. When was the last time you pleaded to see Allah's face with the same earnestness? If not, what is holding you back from making this a constant prayer, starting today?
?
Allah told Musa 'You will not see Me' in this world, but the believers will see Him in the next. Are you living as though that vision is the ultimate goal? Or have you allowed the distractions of this world to make you indifferent to the promise of seeing your Lord? What will you change in your daily life to orient your heart toward that moment?

Certainty in the Prophet and Belief in Eschatological Matters
Sanusi argues for belief in eschatological reports and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why certainty in the Prophet necessitates belief in all eschatological reports and how the objection of observing the dead is answered.

Core Idea
Certainty in the Prophet makes belief in all his reports obligatory, even if we don't witness them.

Sanusi continues by showing the logical consequence of attaining knowledge of the foundations of faith: it leads to certain knowledge of the Prophet's truthfulness, and therefore belief in everything he brought. He then anticipates a doubt about the unseen realities of the grave and death, explaining that these involve violations of normal patterns that are possible and must be believed in their apparent meaning.

Guided Path
1
Trace the logical argument
Notice how Sanusi links the earlier knowledge to the certainty of the Prophet's message and then to obligation of belief in all details.
The structure is conditional: 'if you are granted… then you will attain… so belief becomes obligatory.'
2
Identify the listed eschatological events
The passage lists key events: Gathering, Resurrection, Bridge, Balance, Paradise, Hell, grave punishment and questioning. Commit these to memory as part of the samiyyat.
3
Understand the objection and its refutation
Sanusi addresses the doubt that we see the dead unchanged. He explains that death involves khawariq al-'adat (violations of norms) that are possible and reported by Shari'ah, so we believe them as they are.
This shows the principle of accepting reports about the unseen even if they seem contrary to normal observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا وُفِّقْتَ لعلم هذا كله حصلَ لكَ العلمُ ضرورةً بصدق رسالة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ فوجبَ الإيمانُ بهِ في كلِّ ما جاءَ بهِ عنِ الله سبحانه جملةً وتفصيلاً؛ كالحشر والنشر، والصراط والميزان، والجنة والنار، وعذاب القبر وسؤالِهِ. ولا يقدح فيه مشاهدتُنا للميت على نحو ما وُضِعَ في قبره؛ لأنَّ في الموتِ وما بعده خوارق عاداتٍ أخبر بها الشرع، وهي جائزة، فوجب الإيمان بها على ظاهرها. أما ما استحال ظاهرُهُ؛ نحو: ﴿ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى﴾ [ طه : ٥] فإنَّا نصرفه عن ظاهرِهِ اتفاقاً، ثم إِنْ كانَ لهُ تأويل واحدٌ تعيَّنَ الحمل عليهِ، وإلا وجبَ التفويض مع التنزيه، وهو مذهب الأقدمين، خلافاً لإمام الحرمين
So if you are granted success in knowing all of this, you will necessarily attain knowledge of the truth of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him), so belief in him becomes obligatory in everything he brought from God, Exalted is He, in general and in detail; such as the Gathering and the Resurrection, the Bridge and the Balance, Paradise and Hell, the punishment of the grave and its questioning. And our observation of the dead in the state in which he was placed in his grave does not detract from it; because in death and what follows there are violations of customary norms (khawāriq al-ʿādāt) that the Sharīʿah has informed about, and they are possible, so belief in them is obligatory according to their apparent meaning. As for that whose apparent meaning is impossible, such as {He established Himself over the Throne} [Ṭā Hā 20:5], we indeed divert it from its apparent meaning by consensus. Then if it has a single interpretation (taʾwīl), that interpretation is determined as the one to be applied; otherwise, consignment (tafwīḍ) along with transcendence (tanzīh) becomes obligatory, and this is the way of the early generations (madhhab al-aqdamīn), contrary to Imām al-Ḥaramayn.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the necessity of believing in all eschatological reports brought by the Prophet, followed by a clarification of how to handle ambiguous verses. The author first states that if one attains certainty in the Prophet's truthfulness, belief becomes obligatory in everything he reported from God, both generally and in detail, listing key eschatological events: the Gathering, the Resurrection, the Bridge, the Balance, Paradise, Hell, and the punishment of the grave and its questioning. Then he addresses a potential objection: the fact that we see the dead placed in their graves unchanged does not contradict reports of grave punishment or questioning, because death involves violations of normal patterns (khawāriq al-ʿādāt) that are possible and must be believed in their apparent sense. Next, he turns to verses whose apparent meaning is impossible, such as 'Istawā ʿalā al-ʿArsh' (He established Himself over the Throne). He explains that there is consensus on diverting such verses from their literal meaning. If there is a single valid interpretation (taʾwīl), that interpretation must be adopted. If there is no single agreed interpretation, the obligatory course is tafwīḍ (consigning the true meaning to God) while affirming tanzīh (transcendence of God). This, he says, is the way of the early generations (madhhab al-aqdamīn), contrary to Imām al-Ḥaramayn, who held a different position.

Key Terms
جملة وتفصيلا
خوارق عادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding reports of grave punishment and questioning?
A) They are metaphorical
B) They must be believed in their apparent meaning because they are possible
C) They are rejected because we see the dead unchanged
D) They are only for scholars

Key Takeaway
Belief in all eschatological reports is obligatory once certainty in the Prophet is established, and the fact that we do not observe them is not a valid objection because death involves exceptions to normal patterns.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is my belief in the Prophet such that I accept all his reports—even those about the unseen—without hesitation, or do I find myself mentally resisting some because they seem strange to my experience? What would it take for me to truly submit to every detail he brought?
?
When I see the dead buried in the ground, part of me might doubt the reality of the grave's torment because I see nothing happening. Do I allow my sensory observations to weaken my conviction in what the Prophet informed us? What step will I take today to affirm that God's power transcends what I see?
?
The passage says belief in the Prophet obligates belief in all he brought 'in detail.' Is there any specific eschatological matter—like the Bridge, the Balance, or the punishment of the grave—that I have glossed over or not taken seriously? Am I willing to let this lesson change that starting now?

Handling Ambiguous Verses: Ta'wil and Tafwid
Sanusi explains the treatment of mutashabihat verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct method for dealing with Quranic verses whose apparent meaning seems impossible, and the difference between ta'wil and tafwid.

Core Idea
When a verse's literal meaning is impossible, we divert it by consensus, then either adopt a single interpretation or consign the meaning to God.

Having established the necessity of believing in all reports from the Prophet, Sanusi now addresses a potential difficulty: some Quranic verses and hadiths appear to ascribe physical attributes to God, which is impossible. He explains the agreed-upon method of diverting such verses from their literal meaning and the subsequent options of ta'wil (interpretation) or tafwid (consignment) along with tanzih (transcendence). He also notes that the position of the early generations is tafwid, contrary to Imam al-Haramayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of verses
Sanusi refers to verses whose apparent meaning is impossible, like 'istawa' over the Throne. Recognize that this is a distinct category from the previous reports about the grave.
The phrase 'impossible apparent meaning' is key.
2
Understand the consensus on diversion
There is agreement (ittifaq) that we must divert such verses from their literal sense. This is the first step.
3
Distinguish between ta'wil and tafwid
If there is a single valid interpretation (ta'wil), we adopt it. Otherwise, the obligation is tafwid (consignment) along with tanzih (transcendence). This is the madhhab of the early generations, as opposed to Imam al-Haramayn who may have preferred ta'wil.
Learn the Arabic terms: ta'wil, tafwid, tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا وُفِّقْتَ لعلم هذا كله حصلَ لكَ العلمُ ضرورةً بصدق رسالة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ فوجبَ الإيمانُ بهِ في كلِّ ما جاءَ بهِ عنِ الله سبحانه جملةً وتفصيلاً؛ كالحشر والنشر، والصراط والميزان، والجنة والنار، وعذاب القبر وسؤالِهِ. ولا يقدح فيه مشاهدتُنا للميت على نحو ما وُضِعَ في قبره؛ لأنَّ في الموتِ وما بعده خوارق عاداتٍ أخبر بها الشرع، وهي جائزة، فوجب الإيمان بها على ظاهرها. أما ما استحال ظاهرُهُ؛ نحو: ﴿ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى﴾ [ طه : ٥] فإنَّا نصرفه عن ظاهرِهِ اتفاقاً، ثم إِنْ كانَ لهُ تأويل واحدٌ تعيَّنَ الحمل عليهِ، وإلا وجبَ التفويض مع التنزيه، وهو مذهب الأقدمين، خلافاً لإمام الحرمين
So if you are granted success in knowing all of this, you will necessarily attain knowledge of the truth of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him), so belief in him becomes obligatory in everything he brought from God, Exalted is He, in general and in detail; such as the Gathering and the Resurrection, the Bridge and the Balance, Paradise and Hell, the punishment of the grave and its questioning. And our observation of the dead in the state in which he was placed in his grave does not detract from it; because in death and what follows there are violations of customary norms (khawāriq al-ʿādāt) that the Sharīʿah has informed about, and they are possible, so belief in them is obligatory according to their apparent meaning. As for that whose apparent meaning is impossible, such as {He established Himself over the Throne} [Ṭā Hā 20:5], we indeed divert it from its apparent meaning by consensus. Then if it has a single interpretation (taʾwīl), that interpretation is determined as the one to be applied; otherwise, consignment (tafwīḍ) along with transcendence (tanzīh) becomes obligatory, and this is the way of the early generations (madhhab al-aqdamīn), contrary to Imām al-Ḥaramayn.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the necessity of believing in all eschatological reports brought by the Prophet, followed by a clarification of how to handle ambiguous verses. The author first states that if one attains certainty in the Prophet's truthfulness, belief becomes obligatory in everything he reported from God, both generally and in detail, listing key eschatological events: the Gathering, the Resurrection, the Bridge, the Balance, Paradise, Hell, and the punishment of the grave and its questioning. Then he addresses a potential objection: the fact that we see the dead placed in their graves unchanged does not contradict reports of grave punishment or questioning, because death involves violations of normal patterns (khawāriq al-ʿādāt) that are possible and must be believed in their apparent sense. Next, he turns to verses whose apparent meaning is impossible, such as 'Istawā ʿalā al-ʿArsh' (He established Himself over the Throne). He explains that there is consensus on diverting such verses from their literal meaning. If there is a single valid interpretation (taʾwīl), that interpretation must be adopted. If there is no single agreed interpretation, the obligatory course is tafwīḍ (consigning the true meaning to God) while affirming tanzīh (transcendence of God). This, he says, is the way of the early generations (madhhab al-aqdamīn), contrary to Imām al-Ḥaramayn, who held a different position.

Key Terms
ظاهر
تأويل
تفويض
تنزيه
مذهب الأقدمين
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The early generations always interpreted ambiguous verses metaphorically (ta'wil).
Correction: The passage states that the madhhab of the early generations is tafwid (consignment) along with tanzih, not ta'wil, unless a single interpretation is established.

Checkpoint
What is the way of the early generations (madhhab al-aqdamīn) regarding verses with impossible apparent meaning?
A) Always interpret metaphorically
B) Consign the meaning to God (tafwid) with transcendence
C) Reject the verse
D) Believe it literally

Key Takeaway
The method for handling mutashabihat verses is to divert from the literal meaning by consensus, then either adopt a single valid interpretation or consign the meaning to God while affirming His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse you do not fully understand, do you feel anxious to find an interpretation, or can you humbly say 'Allahu a'lam'? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in God's wisdom versus your own intellect?
?
The early generations were content to consign the meaning of ambiguous verses to God. Is your heart genuinely at peace with not knowing everything about Allah? If not, what is the source of that discomfort, and how might it affect your relationship with Him?
?
Have you ever forced an interpretation onto a verse just to satisfy your curiosity or to seem knowledgeable? How might that be a subtle form of disrespect, and what step can you take today to practice tafwid in your own study of the Qur'an?

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
Belief in Eschatological Realities: Intercession, Basin, and Scrolls
Sanusi lists specific eschatological beliefs including intercession, Basin, and scrolls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific unseen matters that Sanusi lists, including the execution of the threat, intercession, the Basin, and the flying of scrolls, and their basis in scripture.

Core Idea
Eschatological beliefs like the Basin and intercession are known by necessity from the religion.

Sanusi continues his enumeration of matters that must be believed from the unseen. In this passage, he lists several key eschatological events, some with debated details. The passage serves as both a summary and a reminder that these beliefs are firmly grounded in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the list of items and the mention of differing opinions.
The passage uses the phrase 'and among what he brought' to introduce obligatory beliefs.
2
Identify each item in the list
List the specific unseen matters mentioned: execution of the threat on sinners, intercession, the Basin, the Bridge, and flying scrolls. Note the discussion about one or two Basins.
The author indicates the correct view about the Basin.
3
Reflect on 'known by necessity'
Consider what it means that these matters are known from the religion by necessity. Why does Sanusi add that their detailed knowledge is in the Book, Sunnah, and scholars' works?
This emphasizes that these are not obscure but clear, established truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممَّا جَاءَ بهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ويجب الإيمانُ بهِ : نفوذ الوعيدِ في طائفة مِنْ عُصاةِ أُمَّتِهِ، ثم يخرجونَ بشفاعتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ، والحوضُ، وهل هو قبل الصراطِ أو بعده، أو هما حوضانِ: أحدهما قبل الصراطِ، والآخرُ بعده، وهو الصحيحُ ؟ أقوال، وتطاير الصحف، إلى غيرِ ذلكَ ممَّا عُلِمَ مِنَ الدين ضرورةً، وعلمُهُ مُفصَّل في الكتابِ والسنَّةِ وكتب علماء الأمة
And among what he (peace and blessings be upon him) brought and belief in which is obligatory: the execution of the threat (nafadh al-waʿīd) upon a group of the disobedient among his community, then they will come out by his intercession (peace and blessings be upon him); and the Basin (al-Ḥawḍ); and whether it is before the Bridge or after, or there are two Basins: one before the Bridge and the other after it – and that is the correct view – there are opinions; and the flying of the scrolls (taṭāyur al-ṣuḥuf); and other things that are known from the religion by necessity, and their detailed knowledge is in the Book, the Sunnah, and the books of the scholars of the community.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a list of specific unseen matters that must be believed, as part of the section on al-ghaybiyyāt. It begins by stating that among the things brought by the Prophet and obligatory to believe is the execution of the threat (nafadh al-waʿīd) upon a group of sinful believers – meaning that they will be punished in Hell but eventually brought out. This occurs through the Prophet's intercession. Next is the Basin (al-Ḥawḍ), and the author mentions differing opinions about its timing relative to the Bridge (al-Ṣirāṭ): whether it is before, after, or there are two Basins – one before and one after the Bridge. He indicates that the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ) is that there are two Basins. Then he mentions the flying of the scrolls (taṭāyur al-ṣuḥuf), referring to the records of deeds. He concludes by saying that these and other such matters are known from the religion by necessity (ḍarūrah) and their detailed knowledge is found in the Qur'an, Sunnah, and the books of the scholars.

Key Terms
نفوذ الوعيد
شفاعة
الحوض
الصراط
تطاير الصحف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might believe there is only one Basin (al-Ḥawḍ) that is either before or after the Bridge (al-Ṣirāṭ) exclusively.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the correct view is that there are two Basins: one before the Bridge and one after it.

Checkpoint
What is the correct view about the Basin (al-Hawd) according to this passage?
A) It is only before the Bridge
B) It is only after the Bridge
C) There are two Basins: one before and one after
D) It does not exist

Key Takeaway
Sanusi affirms that these eschatological beliefs are obligatory and known by necessity, with details in revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's intercession is only for those sinners who are first punished. Are you living as though you expect to need that intercession, or are you assuming you will never face the threat of punishment? What must change in your life today so that you are not among those who rely solely on intercession without repentance?
?
The existence of two Basins—one before the Bridge and one after—implies a journey of purification. Are you quenching your spiritual thirst now with the water of faith, or will you arrive at that Day parched? What is one habit you can abandon to make your heart more ready for that encounter?
?
Your deeds are recorded in a scroll that will fly to you on the Day of Judgment. If that scroll were opened today, would you be ashamed or proud? What is one deed you can commit to today that you would want to see on that scroll?

Required Beliefs about the Unseen
Sanusi enumerates specific unseen beliefs that are obligatory to accept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific unseen matters that Sanusi says must be believed, including the execution of the threat, the Basin, the Bridge, and the scattering of scrolls.

Core Idea
Belief in the unseen requires accepting specific eschatological events detailed in revelation.

Sanusi concludes his creed by listing essential beliefs about the unseen that are known necessarily from the religion. These include events after death and on the Day of Judgment. In this lesson, we will explore what he mentions and why they are considered necessary knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on unseen matters
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's enumeration come through.
2
Identify each item
List the specific items: nufudh al-wa'id, al-hawd, al-sirat, tathayyur al-suhuf. Notice that Sanusi discusses different opinions about the Basin and the Bridge.
He indicates that the correct view is two basins.
3
Reflect on 'known necessarily from the religion'
Ask yourself what it means for these matters to be known 'bi al-darura' (necessarily). This means they are so clearly established that denying them is disbelief.
This concept ties back to earlier lessons on daruriyyat.

Section
On explaining a summary of what must be believed from the unseen matters
that are known from the religion necessarily or nearly so.
And among what the Messenger (peace be upon him) brought and must be believed: the execution of the threat (nufudh al-wa'id) upon a group of the sinners of his community, then they come out through his intercession (peace be upon him), and the Basin (al-hawd), and whether it is before the Bridge (al-sirat) or after it, or there are two basins: one before the Bridge and the other after it, and that is the correct one? — opinions, and the scattering of the scrolls (tathayyur al-suhuf), and other matters that are known from the religion necessarily, and their detailed knowledge is in the Book, the Sunnah, and the books of the scholars of the community.
And know: that the sources of rulings from which we derive are: the Book,
and the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community (ijma' al-umma), and the analogy of the imams (qiyas al-a'imma).
And following the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-salih) and tracing their footsteps is salvation for whoever clings to it.
And the best of people after our Prophet (peace be upon him) are: Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, and the chosen position of Malik is: suspending judgment (al-waqf) regarding 'Uthman and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both and with those before them).
And all the Companions are just imams; whichever of them you follow, you are guided.
May Allah benefit us through love of them, cause us to die upon their way, and gather us in
their company, Amen, O Lord of the worlds.
This is "The Creed of the People of Tawhid" (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid), which, by the favor of Allah, brings one out of the darkness of ignorance and imitation, and humbles, with Allah's help, the nose of every obstinate innovator. We ask Him, exalted, to benefit by it through His favor, and to expand the breast of everyone who strives to acquire it through His bounty.
And may Allah bless our master and patron Muhammad as many times as the number of those who remember You and remember him, and as many times as the number of those who are heedless of Your remembrance and of his remembrance, and may Allah be pleased with his family and Companions, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of Sanusi's creed (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid). It serves as a summary of required beliefs about the unseen that are known necessarily from the religion, followed by the sources of Islamic rulings, the virtue of the first two caliphs, the justice of all Companions, and a closing prayer.

First, he lists specific unseen matters that must be believed: the execution of the threat (al-wa'id) upon sinful Muslims, meaning that some will be punished in Hell but then brought out through the Prophet's intercession; the Basin (al-hawd), with a discussion of its timing relative to the Bridge (al-sirat) — he mentions different opinions but indicates that the correct view is that there are two basins, one before the Bridge and one after. He also mentions the scattering of scrolls (tathayyur al-suhuf), referring to the recording of deeds. He then says these and other matters are known necessarily from the religion, and their detailed knowledge is found in the Quran, Sunnah, and books of scholars.

Second, he states the four sources of Islamic rulings: the Quran, the Sunnah, the consensus of the community (ijma'), and the analogy of the imams (qiyas). This is the standard methodology of Sunni jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh). He adds that following the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-salih) and tracing their footsteps is salvation for whoever clings to it.

Third, he affirms the superiority of Abu Bakr then 'Umar after the Prophet, which is the Sunni consensus. He also notes that Imam Malik's chosen position is to suspend judgment (al-waqf) regarding which of 'Uthman and 'Ali is better — this reflects the cautious attitude of some early scholars regarding disputes between Companions.

Fourth, he declares that all Companions are just (udul) and are imams; following any of them guides one rightly.

Finally, he praises the creed he has written, calling it "The Creed of the People of Tawhid" (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid), and prays that Allah benefit people through it and protect them from innovation. The passage ends with a blessing upon the Prophet and praise to Allah.

Key Terms
نفوذ الوعيد (nufudh al-wa'id)
الحوض (al-hawd)
الصراط (al-sirat)
تطاير الصحف (tathayyur al-suhuf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the 'execution of the threat' means all sinners will be punished eternally, or that intercession does not occur.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that the threat is executed on a group ('faith-ta'), but then they are brought out through intercession, affirming both punishment and intercession for sinful Muslims.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, which of the following is NOT explicitly listed as a required belief from the unseen?
A) The execution of the threat upon sinful Muslims
B) The Basin (al-hawd)
C) The splitting of the moon
D) The scattering of the scrolls

Key Takeaway
Belief in specific eschatological events such as the intercession, the Basin, the Bridge, and the scrolls is obligatory because they are known necessarily from the religion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live with the certainty that your deeds will be scattered as scrolls and you will be held accountable? What single change would you make today if you truly believed that?
?
The Prophet's intercession is for a group of sinful Muslims. Are you confident that you will be among those worthy of that intercession? What steps are you taking now to ensure you are not among those who are beyond it?
?
The debate about the Basin and Bridge might seem technical, but it reminds us that the Hereafter is real and close. If you knew you would stand before the Basin tomorrow, what would you do differently today?

Sources of Islamic Rulings and Following the Salaf
Sanusi states the four sources of law and the virtue of following the salaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four sources of Islamic rulings according to Sanusi and the importance of following the righteous predecessors.

Core Idea
Islamic law derives from Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy; following the salaf is salvation.

After discussing beliefs about the unseen, Sanusi turns to the methodology of deriving Islamic rulings. He lists the four foundational sources and emphasizes the importance of adhering to the way of the early generations. This lesson explains these sources and the concept of following the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sources and salaf
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that Sanusi uses the phrase 'وأن أصول الأحكام التي منها نتلقى' (the sources of rulings from which we derive).
2
Understand the four sources
Identify each source: al-Kitab (Quran), al-Sunna, Ijma' al-umma (consensus), Qiyas al-a'imma (analogy of the imams). Understand why each is a source.
Qiyas is attributed to the imams because they are qualified to perform analogy.
3
Reflect on following the salaf
Sanusi says 'following the righteous predecessors and tracing their footsteps is salvation for whoever clings to it.' Think about what this means for methodology and avoiding innovation.
This is a key principle of Sunni orthodoxy: the way of the salaf is the saved path.

?

The Virtue of the Companions and Conclusion
Sanusi affirms the precedence of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, suspends judgment on 'Uthman and 'Ali, and declares all Companions just.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's affirmation of the superiority of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, the suspension of judgment regarding 'Uthman and 'Ali, and the justice of all Companions.

Core Idea
The best after the Prophet are Abu Bakr then 'Umar; all Companions are just and worthy of following.

Sanusi concludes his creed by addressing the rank of the first two caliphs, the stance of Imam Malik regarding 'Uthman and 'Ali, and the general justice of all Companions. He also includes a final prayer and the title of his work. This lesson covers these important points about the Companions and the closing of the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the companions
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the three parts: best of people after the Prophet, the waqf position on 'Uthman and 'Ali, and the justice of all Companions.
2
Understand the hierarchy
Sanusi states that after the Prophet, the best is Abu Bakr, then 'Umar. Then he mentions that Malik's chosen position is waqf (suspending judgment) regarding 'Uthman and 'Ali. Why would Malik do that?
Waqf does not mean doubting their faith, but rather not declaring which of them is superior, due to potential fitna.
3
Reflect on the justice of all Companions
Sanusi says all Companions are 'udul (just) and 'a'imma (imams) - a key Sunni principle that safeguards their integrity and makes their narrations and example reliable.
Then read the closing supplication and title of the creed.

فصل
في بيان جملةٍ ممَّا يجب الإيمانُ بِهِ مِنَ الغيوب
ممَّا عُلِمَ مِنَ الدين بالضرورة أو شبهها
وممَّا جَاءَ بهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ويجب الإيمانُ بهِ : نفوذ الوعيدِ في طائفة مِنْ عُصاةِ أُمَّتِهِ ، ثم يخرجونَ بشفاعتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، والحوضُ ، وهل هو قبل الصراطِ أو بعده ، أو هما حوضانِ : أحدهما قبل الصراطِ ، والآخرُ بعده ، وهو الصحيحُ ؟ أقوال ، وتطاير الصحف ، إلى غيرِ ذلكَ ممَّا عُلِمَ مِنَ الدين ضرورةً ، وعلمُهُ مُفصَّل في الكتابِ والسنَّةِ وكتب علماء الأمة
واعلم : أنَّ أصول الأحكام التي منها نتلقى : الكتاب ،
والسنَّةُ ، وإجماع الأمة ، وقياس الأئمة ..
واتباع السلف الصالح واقتفاء آثَارِهِم نجاةٌ لَمَنْ تمسَّكَ به
وأفضلُ الناس بعد نبينا صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ : أبو بكرٍ ، ثم عمرُ ، ومختارُ مالكِ : الوقفُ فيما بينَ عثمانَ وعلي رضيَ الله تعالى عنهما وعمَّنْ قبلهما
والصحابة كلهم عدول أئمة ، بأيهم اقتديتم اهتديتم ،
نفعنا الله بمحبَّتِهم ، وأماتنا على سُنَّتِهم ، وحشرنا في
زمرتهم ، آمين يا ربَّ العالمين .
فهذه « عقيدة أهل التوحيدِ » ، المُخرِجةُ بفضلِ اللهِ تعالى مِنْ ظلماتِ الجهل والتقليدِ ، المُرغِمةُ بعونِ اللهِ أَنفَ كل مبتدع عنيد ، نسأله سبحانَهُ أنْ ينفع بها بفضلِهِ ، ويشرح بها صدرَ كلَّ مَنْ يسعى في تحصيلها بطَوْلِهِ
وصل اللهم على سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد عدد ما ذكرَكَ وذكره الذاكرونَ ، وعدد ما غفل عن ذكرِكَ وذكره الغافلونَ ، ورضي الله عن آلِهِ وصحبه ، والحمدُ للهِ ربِّ
al عالمين .
Section
On explaining a summary of what must be believed from the unseen matters
that are known from the religion necessarily or nearly so.
And among what the Messenger (peace be upon him) brought and must be believed: the execution of the threat (nufudh al-wa'id) upon a group of the sinners of his community, then they come out through his intercession (peace be upon him), and the Basin (al-hawd), and whether it is before the Bridge (al-sirat) or after it, or there are two basins: one before the Bridge and the other after it, and that is the correct one? — opinions, and the scattering of the scrolls (tathayyur al-suhuf), and other matters that are known from the religion necessarily, and their detailed knowledge is in the Book, the Sunnah, and the books of the scholars of the community.
And know: that the sources of rulings from which we derive are: the Book,
and the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community (ijma' al-umma), and the analogy of the imams (qiyas al-a'imma).
And following the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-salih) and tracing their footsteps is salvation for whoever clings to it.
And the best of people after our Prophet (peace be upon him) are: Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, and the chosen position of Malik is: suspending judgment (al-waqf) regarding 'Uthman and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both and with those before them).
And all the Companions are just imams; whichever of them you follow, you are guided.
May Allah benefit us through love of them, cause us to die upon their way, and gather us in
their company, Amen, O Lord of the worlds.
This is "The Creed of the People of Tawhid" (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid), which, by the favor of Allah, brings one out of the darkness of ignorance and imitation, and humbles, with Allah's help, the nose of every obstinate innovator. We ask Him, exalted, to benefit by it through His favor, and to expand the breast of everyone who strives to acquire it through His bounty.
And may Allah bless our master and patron Muhammad as many times as the number of those who remember You and remember him, and as many times as the number of those who are heedless of Your remembrance and of his remembrance, and may Allah be pleased with his family and Companions, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is the concluding section of Sanusi's creed (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid). It serves as a summary of required beliefs about the unseen that are known necessarily from the religion, followed by the sources of Islamic rulings, the virtue of the first two caliphs, the justice of all Companions, and a closing prayer.

First, he lists specific unseen matters that must be believed: the execution of the threat (al-wa'id) upon sinful Muslims, meaning that some will be punished in Hell but then brought out through the Prophet's intercession; the Basin (al-hawd), with a discussion of its timing relative to the Bridge (al-sirat) — he mentions different opinions but indicates that the correct view is that there are two basins, one before the Bridge and one after. He also mentions the scattering of scrolls (tathayyur al-suhuf), referring to the recording of deeds. He then says these and other matters are known necessarily from the religion, and their detailed knowledge is found in the Quran, Sunnah, and books of scholars.

Second, he states the four sources of Islamic rulings: the Quran, the Sunnah, the consensus of the community (ijma'), and the analogy of the imams (qiyas). This is the standard methodology of Sunni jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh). He adds that following the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-salih) and tracing their footsteps is salvation for whoever clings to it.

Third, he affirms the superiority of Abu Bakr then 'Umar after the Prophet, which is the Sunni consensus. He also notes that Imam Malik's chosen position is to suspend judgment (al-waqf) regarding which of 'Uthman and 'Ali is better — this reflects the cautious attitude of some early scholars regarding disputes between Companions.

Fourth, he declares that all Companions are just (udul) and are imams; following any of them guides one rightly.

Finally, he praises the creed he has written, calling it "The Creed of the People of Tawhid" (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid), and prays that Allah benefit people through it and protect them from innovation. The passage ends with a blessing upon the Prophet and praise to Allah.

Key Terms
الوقف (al-waqf)
عقيدة أهل التوحيد (Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that suspending judgment (waqf) implies doubt about the faith or caliphate of 'Uthman and 'Ali.
Correction: Waqf only pertains to which of the two is superior, not to their righteousness or legitimacy. The passage affirms that all Companions are just and imams.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, who are the best two people after the Prophet?
A) Abu Bakr and 'Umar
B) 'Uthman and 'Ali
C) The two in order: Abu Bakr then 'Umar
D) All four caliphs equally

Key Takeaway
The best after the Prophet are Abu Bakr then 'Umar; all Companions are just imams; and suspending judgment on the superiority of 'Uthman and 'Ali is a valid position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear Muslims dispute the virtues of 'Uthman and 'Ali, is your heart attached to a faction? Are you willing to suspend judgment as Sanusi teaches, or does pride prevent you from being neutral? Today, pray for the love of all Companions and commit to silence where the Salaf were silent.
?
Sanusi prays to die upon the way of the Companions. Is your daily life aligned with their sunnah? Look at your habits, your speech, your priorities—how far are you from the path of those who were with the Prophet? Ask yourself: if I die tonight, would I be resurrected among them?
?
You call yourself a follower of Ahl al-Tawhid, but do you truly submit your intellect to the creed of the Salaf? Where do you still cling to personal opinion or blind imitation? Sanusi says this creed 'emerges from ignorance and imitation'—examine one area where you are still imitating without understanding and resolve to learn the proof today.

Scriptural Evidence for the Necessity of Knowledge
The author cites Quranic verses and hadiths proving that knowledge is required for faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and Sunnah command knowledge (ʿilm) rather than mere belief (iʿtiqād) in matters of faith, and how the author uses specific verses and hadiths to establish this.

Core Idea
The Quran commands 'know,' not 'believe' — knowledge is the foundation of faith.

This passage presents the scriptural evidence for the position that true faith requires knowledge grounded in evidence, not blind acceptance. The author cites several Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths to demonstrate that the term 'knowledge' is consistently used where one might expect 'belief,' and that certainty (yaqīn) and insight (baṣīra) are synonymous with knowledge. Understanding this evidence is crucial for grasping the rationalist methodology of Ashʿarī theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic citations
Read the first set of verses carefully, noting the repeated command 'know' (faʿlamū). Reflect on the difference between knowledge and belief as highlighted by the author.
2
Analyze the logical inference from the hadith
Consider the first hadith: Allah commands believing servants with what He commanded messenger servants. Since messengers cannot rely on taqlīd, believers must also avoid taqlīd.
3
Define key terms
The author defines 'baṣīra' as knowledge of truth by its evidence. Note how 'yaqīn' is equated with knowledge.
4
Understand the contrapositive argument
The author applies the contrapositive (ʿaks al-naqīḍ) to the verse about insight: if one is not upon insight, he is not truly following the Prophet, and thus not a believer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلتُ : ويدلُّ على مذهب الجمهور : قوله تعالى : ﴿ فَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا أُنزِلَ بِعِلْمِ اللَّهِ وَأَن لَّا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ﴾ [هود : ١٤] ، فأمر بالعلم لا بالاعتقادِ ،
وقد علمت الفرق بينهما (۱) ، وقولُهُ : فَاعلَم أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ [محمد : ١٩] ، وقولُهُ : لِتَعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ أَحَاطَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عِلماً ﴾ [الطلاق : ۱۲] ، وقوله : لِيَسْتَيْقِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ وَيَزْدَادَ الَّذِينَ امنوا ايمننا ﴾ [المدثر : ۳۱] ، واليقين بمعنى العلم ، وقوله : ﴿ قُلْ هَذِهِ سَبِيلِي أَدْعُوا إِلَى اللهِ عَلَى بَصِيرَةٍ أَنَا وَمَنِ اتَّبَعَنِي ﴾ [يوسف : ١٠٨] ، والبصيرة : معرفةُ الحقِّ بدليلِهِ ، فمَنْ لم يكن على بصيرةٍ في عَقْدِهِ لم يكن مُتَّبعاً للنبي صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ عملاً بمقتضى عكس النقيض الموافق(٢) ، فلا يكون مؤمنا (۳)

ويدلُّ عليه أيضاً : قوله صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( إِنَّ اللهَ أَمَرَ عِبَادَهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ بِمَا أَمَرَ بِهِ عِبَادَهُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ (٤) ، ومعلوم أنَّ التقليد لا يصح في حق المرسلين ، وقولُه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( مَنْ مَاتَ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ « أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ. . دخَلَ الْجَنَّةَ (٥) ، ولم يقل : وهو يعتقد

وكلُّ آية في القرآنِ ذامَّةٍ للتقليد ، وآمرة بالنظر والاعتبار .. دليل على ذلكَ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ قُلِ انْظُرُوا ﴾ [يونس : ١٠١] ، وقوله جلَّ
I say: And it indicates the position of the majority: His statement the Most High: {So know that what was sent down with the knowledge of Allah and that there is no god but He} [Hud:14]; He commanded knowledge not belief. And you have known the difference between them (1). And His statement: {So know that there is no god but Allah} [Muhammad:19]; And His statement: {That you may know that Allah is over all things competent and that Allah has encompassed all things in knowledge} [Talaq:12]; And His statement: {That those who were given the Scripture may be certain and those who believe may increase in faith} [Muddaththir:31]; and certainty is in the sense of knowledge. And His statement: {Say, 'This is my way; I invite to Allah with insight, I and those who follow me'} [Yusuf:108]; and insight is knowledge of truth by its evidence. So whoever is not upon insight in his creed, he is not a follower of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم, by applying the contrapositive (2), thus he is not a believer (3). And it also indicates: his statement صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Indeed Allah commanded His believing servants with what He commanded His messenger servants' (4), and it is known that taqlīd is not valid for messengers. And his statement صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'Whoever dies while knowing that there is no god but Allah enters Paradise' (5), and he did not say: while believing. And every verse in the Quran that blames taqlīd and commands reflection and consideration is evidence for that; such as His statement the Most High: {Say, 'Look'} [Yunus:101] and His statement the Most High...
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage provides textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah to support the position that knowledge (ʿilm) is required for faith, not mere belief. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses. First, verse [Hud 14] commands 'know' (faʿlamū), not 'believe', indicating that knowledge is the required state. The author notes that the reader already knows the difference between knowledge and belief. Second, verse [Muhammad 19] similarly commands 'know'. Third, verse [Talaq 12] says 'that you may know', emphasizing the purpose of creation and revelation is knowledge. Fourth, verse [Muddaththir 31] uses 'liyastaqīna' (to be certain), which the author explains is synonymous with knowledge. Fifth, verse [Yusuf 108] uses 'baṣīra' (insight), which the author defines as knowledge of truth by its evidence. The author draws a logical consequence: whoever is not upon insight in his creed is not truly following the Prophet, using the contrapositive (ʿaks al-naqīḍ), and thus is not a believer. Then the author adds hadith evidence. The first hadith states that Allah has commanded believing servants with what He commanded His messenger servants; it is known that messengers cannot rely on taqlīd, so believers must also not rely on taqlīd. The second hadith states that whoever dies while knowing 'there is no god but Allah' enters Paradise; the Prophet said 'knowing' not 'believing', indicating that knowledge is the criterion. The author concludes that every verse condemning taqlīd or commanding reflection supports this position, citing [Yunus 101] as an example. The passage ends abruptly with 'and His statement the Most High' suggesting more evidence was to follow.

Key Terms
علم
بصيرة
تقليد
يقين
نظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that mere belief (iʿtiqād) is sufficient for faith and is the same as knowledge (ʿilm).
Correction: The Quranic verses command 'know' (faʿlamū) and the hadith says 'knowing' (yaʿlamu), showing that knowledge is distinct and required. The author explicitly contrasts knowledge with belief.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the Quranic verse 'Say, this is my way; I invite to Allah with insight'?
A) Insight means spiritual intuition.
B) Insight is knowledge of truth by its evidence.
C) Insight is the same as blind faith.
D) Insight is a special gift for prophets only.

Key Takeaway
The Quran and Sunnah command knowledge (ʿilm) in matters of faith, not mere belief or taqlīd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah,' do you truly know it through your own evidence and reflection, or are you repeating what you've been told? What step will you take this week to deepen your certainty based on insight (baṣīra)?
?
Think of a belief about Allah or the unseen that you hold simply because 'everyone in my family or community says so.' Are you willing to examine it with evidence from the Quran and reason? How would your relationship with Allah change if your faith was built on your own personal knowledge?
?
The Prophet ﷺ said that entering Paradise is tied to 'knowing' la ilaha illa Allah, not just 'believing.' Are you satisfied with inherited faith, or will you strive to make your faith a matter of knowledge? What is one concrete change you will make starting today to move from blind acceptance to informed certainty?

The Danger of Taqlid and the Hypocrite in the Grave
Sanusi explains the danger of taqlid through the analogy of hypocrisy and the grave trial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why blind imitation (taqlid) without inner conviction is akin to hypocrisy and leads to punishment in the grave.

Core Idea
Blind faith without proof leaves the heart sick and the tongue defenseless in the grave.

This lesson reveals a profound warning: simply repeating words of faith without heartfelt certainty is not enough. Sanusi draws a stark comparison between the muqallid (blind follower) and the hypocrite, showing that the same disease of doubt that plagues the heart in this life will expose the soul in the grave. The lesson unpacks the hadith of the two angels and what really saves a person.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the key phrase 'his heart is sick and confused.'
This phrase is central to the analogy.
2
Identify the central analogy
The muqallid is compared to a hypocrite. How are they similar? Both have tongues that say one thing but hearts that are uncertain.
3
Examine the Qur'anic proof
Look at verse 2:10. How does Sanusi use it to support his argument? The heart's disease renders the tongue's confession useless.
Allah says: 'In their hearts is disease, so Allah has increased them disease.'
4
Reflect on the grave scene
The hadith describes the doubter's answer. Why is 'I do not know' fatal? What does this teach about the necessity of certainty?
The angels respond with rebuke and punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعني : أنَّ الضميرَ في ( صاحبها ) يعود على حرفة التقليد ؛ التصميم على العقائدِ بغيرِ تحصينها بالدليل لا يأمن صاحبها ـ على تقدير صحة القولِ بالتقليدِ - مِنْ زوالِهِ عندَ عروض أدنى شبهة . وعلى تقديرِ أنْ يُقابلَ ذلكَ ويكابر نفسَهُ بالتصميم اللساني . .. فأَنَّى ينفعُهُ ذلك والقلبُ الذي هو محلُّ الإيمانِ مريض مُتحيّر يقولُ : لا أدري ؟! فيدخلُ في زمرة المنافقين الذين تخالف ألسنتهم قلوبهم قال الله تعالى في حقهم : ﴿ فِي قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌ فَزَادَهُمُ اللَّهُ مَرَضًا ﴾ [البقرة : ١٠] أي : لمَّا مرضَتْ قلوبهم لم ينتفعوا بما في ألسنتهم ، وهذا المريضُ القلبِ المرتاب هو مِنَ القائلين في القبر عند مساءلة الملكين : لا أدري ، سمعتُ الناسَ يقولونَ شيئاً فقلتُه ، إذ هذا حال قلبه في حياتِهِ وعندَ موتِهِ ، واللسانُ في ذلك الموطن لا يتركُ - كما في الدنيا ـ أنْ يَتشَبَّعَ بما ليس في القلبِ . قال ابنُ دهاق رحمهُ الله ورضي عنه في ( شرح الإرشادِ » لما تكلَّمَ على فتنة الملكين في القبرِ ، وساق الحديث ، وفي آخره : « الْمُنَافِقُ أَوِ الْمُرْتَابُ فَيَقُولُ : لَا أَدْرِي ، سَمِعْتُ النَّاسَ يَقُولُونَ شَيْئاً فَقُلْتُهُ ، فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ : لَا دَرَيْتَ وَلَا تَلَيْتَ ، وَيَضْرِبَانِهِ بِالْمِقْمَعِ مِنَ الْحَدِيدِ ، فَيَصِيحُ صَيْحَةٌ يَسْمَعُهَا كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنْسَ »
He means: that the pronoun in 'its owner' refers to the craft of taqlid; the determination upon beliefs without fortifying them with proof—its owner, assuming the validity of the statement on taqlid—is not safe from its removal at the occurrence of the slightest doubt. And assuming that he confronts that and forces himself with verbal determination... so how can that benefit him while the heart, which is the locus of faith, is sick and confused saying: 'I do not know'?! So he enters into the group of the hypocrites whose tongues contradict their hearts. Allah most high said concerning them: {In their hearts is disease, so Allah has increased them disease} [al-Baqarah: 10], meaning: when their hearts became diseased, they did not benefit from what was on their tongues. And this sick, doubting heart is among those who say in the grave during the questioning of the two angels: 'I do not know; I heard the people saying something so I said it.' For this is the state of his heart in his life and at his death, and the tongue in that situation does not leave off—as in the world—pretending to have what is not in the heart. Ibn Dahaq, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said in his commentary on al-Irshad, when he spoke about the trial of the two angels in the grave, relating the hadith, and at its end: 'The hypocrite or the doubter says: I do not know; I heard people saying something so I said it. Then the two angels say to him: You neither knew nor did you recite [properly], and they strike him with an iron mallet, and he screams a scream that everything hears except the jinn and humans.'
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the previous lesson, unpacking the meaning of 'its owner' (sahibuha). The pronoun refers to 'the craft of taqlid' (hirfat al-taqlid). Sanusi explains that insisting on beliefs without fortifying them with proof—even if one considers taqlid valid—leaves one vulnerable to the removal of that faith at the slightest doubt. If the person tries to resist verbally (bil-tasmim al-lisani), it cannot benefit him because his heart, the seat of faith, is sick and confused, saying 'I do not know.' Such a person joins the hypocrites (munafiqin), whose tongues contradict their hearts. The author quotes Qur'an 2:10 as evidence: when hearts are diseased, the tongue's confession has no benefit. Then he connects this to the grave trial: the doubting heart will answer the angels' question with 'I do not know, I heard people say something so I said it.' This reflects his lifelong lack of inner certainty. Citing Ibn Dahaq in his commentary on al-Irshad, Sanusi recounts the hadith that the hypocrite or doubter will say that, and the angels will rebuke him and strike him with an iron mallet. The key lesson is the absolute necessity of inner conviction rooted in proof, as opposed to mere verbal imitation.

حرفة التقليد
تصميم لساني
منافق
قلب مريض
فتنة الملكين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that merely stating the Shahada verbally is sufficient for salvation.
Correction: This passage shows that hypocrisy and doubt in the heart lead to punishment in the grave, as the doubter's verbal confession does not benefit him.

A) 'I believe in Allah and His Messenger'
B) 'I do not know; I heard people saying something so I said it'
C) 'I was a follower of such-and-such scholar'
D) 'Allah is my Lord'

Key Takeaway
Inner certainty rooted in proof saves a person from the punishment of the grave, not mere verbal repetition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
In what area of your life does your tongue say ‘I believe’ while your heart secretly says ‘I am not sure’? What practical step will you take this week to move from mere imitation to genuine certainty?
?
The passage warns that the tongue in the grave cannot pretend to have what is not in the heart. If you were to die tonight, would your heart be firm or sick? What are you doing right now to fortify your heart with proof before you face the mallet?

The Trial of the Grave and Two Types of Hypocrisy
Sanusi's commentator defines the trial of the grave and classifies hypocrisy into two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the two types of hypocrisy and the critical importance of personal reflection (nazar) over blind imitation (taqlid) for passing the trial of the grave.

Core Idea
Blind imitation breeds hidden hypocrisy that fails the grave's test.

This passage from Sanusi's commentator addresses the grave trial and a hidden danger: hypocrisy that a person himself does not recognize. It teaches that mere imitation of one's environment is insufficient; true faith requires personal reflection on the proofs of prophethood and monotheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the trial of the grave
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the commentator’s warning about the grave trial and the two types of hypocrisy.
Pay attention to the contrast between taqlid and nazar.
2
Identify the two types of hypocrisy
Look for the classification: one type known to the person (like the hypocrites in the Prophet's time) and another not known to the person (hidden hypocrisy from blind imitation).
The second type is subtle and dangerous.
3
Reflect on the role of nazar vs taqlid
Consider why the commentator emphasizes nazar (reflection) and condemns taqlid (blind imitation). This is the core of the lesson.
Nazar leads to conviction; taqlid leads to vulnerability.
4
Connect to the hadith on self-knowledge
The passage ends with 'Whoever knows himself knows his Lord.' Reflect on how self-reflection leads to knowledge of Allah and protects from hidden hypocrisy.
This ties the entire lesson together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( هذه الفتنةُ فتنة القبر لا ينجو منها مَنْ أخذ في دينه بالتقليد وترك النظر في أدلَّةِ الرسالة والتوحيد ، ولذلك قيل : النفاق نفاقانِ : نفاق يعرفُهُ صاحبُهُ مِنْ نفسِهِ ؛ وهو نفاقُ الذين كانوا في عهد النبي صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، ومَنْ في معناهم مِنَ الزنادقة ، ونفاق لا يعرفُهُ صاحبُهُ مِنْ نفسِهِ ؛ وهو أنْ يُولَدَ الرجلُ أو المرأةُ بينَ أبوين مسلمين ، فيسمع قول : لا إله إلا الله ، محمَّدٌ رسولُ اللهِ ، فيقول نحو ما سمع اتباعاً وتقليداً لهم ، حتى لو تُصُوِّرَ أنْ يُولَدَ بين النصارى لَقَالَ مثل أقوالهم اتباعاً لهم وتقليداً في ذلكَ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ ينظر في خلقِهِ ، ومِنْ أي شيءٍ خُلِقَ ، وكيفَ انتقلَ مِنْ طَورٍ إلى طورٍ ، ولذلك قال عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : « مَنْ عَرَفَ نَفْسَهُ عَرَفَ رَبَّهُ (۳) »
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "This trial is the trial of the grave. None escapes it except one who takes up his religion through reflection (nazar) and abandons blind imitation (taqlid), and who considers the proofs of the message and monotheism (tawhid). Therefore it is said: Hypocrisy (nifaq) is of two types: hypocrisy known to its own self – and it is the hypocrisy of those who were in the era of the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) and those similar to them from the heretics (zanadiqa); and hypocrisy not known to its own self – and it is that a man or woman is born between two Muslim parents, so he hears the saying 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' and he says something similar to what he heard out of imitation and blind following of them, so that if he had been imagined to be born among Christians, he would have said similar to their sayings out of imitation and blind following of them, without reflecting upon his creation, and from what thing he was created, and how he moved from stage to stage. Therefore the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) said: 'Whoever knows himself knows his Lord.'"
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the trial of the grave. The author begins by stating that the trial of the grave is a great trial that no one escapes except those who take their religion through reflection (nazar) and abandon blind imitation (taqlid). He then explains that this is because such people have properly considered the proofs of prophethood and tawhid. He then introduces the classification of hypocrisy (nifaq) into two types. The first type is the hypocrisy that the hypocrite himself knows he has; this is the hypocrisy of those who lived in the time of the Prophet and pretended to be Muslims while concealing disbelief, and others like them from the heretics (zanadiqa). The second type is the hypocrisy that the hypocrite himself does not know he has. This occurs when a person is born to Muslim parents, hears the shahada, and merely repeats it out of imitation without any personal reflection or conviction. Such a person, had he been born among Christians, would have similarly repeated their statements out of imitation. The author emphasizes that this person fails to reflect on his own creation and the stages of his development. He then cites the well-known saying (attributed here to the Prophet) "Whoever knows himself knows his Lord," which underscores the importance of self-reflection as a path to knowledge of Allah. This passage warns against the danger of taqlid and the hidden hypocrisy that arises from it, which can lead one to fail the trial of the grave.

Key Terms
فتنة القبر
التقليد
النظر
النفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Simply being born into a Muslim family and repeating the shahada is sufficient for salvation without personal reflection and conviction.
Correction: The passage teaches that such imitation is a form of hidden hypocrisy that fails the trial of the grave. True faith requires nazar (reflection) on the proofs.

Checkpoint

A) Hypocrisy known to its own self
B) Hypocrisy not known to its own self
C) The hypocrisy of the heretics
D) The hypocrisy of the people of the Prophet's era

Key Takeaway
True salvation in the trial of the grave depends on personal reflection and conviction, not inherited imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'La ilaha illa Allah', do you truly reflect on its meaning and the proofs of tawhid, or do you simply repeat it because you were raised among Muslims? What would you say if you had been born among Christians?
?

?
The Prophet said: 'Whoever knows himself knows his Lord.' In what specific ways have you truly reflected on your own creation—your coming into being, your stages of development—to deepen your knowledge of Allah? If you haven't, what is holding you back from starting today?

The Danger of Doubt at Death and in the Grave
A narrative warning about the consequences of neglecting doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Satan exploits a person's neglect of reflection to plant fatal doubts at the moment of death, and how the grave reveals the true state of one's faith.

Core Idea
Unaddressed doubt at death becomes eternal regret.

This passage from the commentary vividly depicts the tragic end of one who follows blind imitation. It shows how Satan uses the person's own avoidance of reflection to attack at the weakest moment—death. Then it reveals the grave's testimony, sealing the person's fate based on what was in their heart.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the narrative sink in before interpreting.
Notice the sequence: living state → death moment → grave.
2
Identify Satan's strategy at death
Find how Satan plants doubt at the moment of death, exploiting the person's history of avoiding reflection. Note the phrase 'when there is no thought'.
The person dies in doubt because he never investigated his doubts in life.
3
Understand the grave's testimony
See how the person's mouth is sealed and he speaks only what he truly believed. Contrast the 'arif' with the 'shakk' (doubter).
The grave reveals the inner reality that was hidden in life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربَّما يمرُّ بباله الفكرُ في خَلْقِ اللهِ ، فيردُّه شيطانُ مِنَ الإِنسِ أَوِ الجنّ ، فيقولُ لهُ : إِنْ تَفَكَّرتَ فقد تشكَّكْتَ ، فيُعْرِضُ عَنِ النظر إلى الموتِ ، فإذا بلغَتِ الروح الحلقوم أتاهُ الشيطانُ في ذلك المضيق حينَ لا فكر ، ويشكّكُهُ في دينِهِ ، فيموتُ على شكهِ والعياذُ باللهِ مِنْ ضروب الشكوك ، فإذا كانَ في القبرِ خُتِمَ على الأفواه ، ونطق بما عندَهُ مِنْ غيرِ زيادة ولا نقصان ، فإنْ كانَ عارفاً نطق بالحقِّ ، وإنْ كانَ شاكاً غيرَ عالم قال : لا أدري ، وكذلك كان يقولُ بقلبه في حياتِهِ : لا أدري ، وكانَ يَطرُقُهُ الشكُ أحياناً ، فلا يبحث عليه(۱) ، ولا يداوي سَقام سريرته ، فإذا مات لحقَهُ الندم حينَ لا ينفعُهُ ، واعتذرَ إلى مَنْ لا يسمعُهُ ، وهلكَ والعياذُ باللهِ مِنْ سخط الله تعالى ((۲)
Perhaps the thought of Allah's creation passes his mind, but a devil (shaytan) from humans or jinn repels him, saying: "If you reflect, you will doubt." So he turns away from reflecting on death. When the soul reaches the throat, Satan comes to him in that narrow strait when there is no thought, and he makes him doubt his religion, so he dies in his doubt – we seek refuge with Allah from the kinds of doubts. Then when he is in the grave, mouths are sealed, and he speaks according to what he has without increase or decrease. If he is a knower (arif), he speaks the truth; but if he is a doubter without knowledge, he says: "I do not know." And such was his heart's utterance in his life: "I do not know." Doubt used to strike him sometimes, but he did not investigate it, nor did he cure the sickness of his conscience. So when he died, regret overtakes him when it does not benefit him, and he apologizes to one who does not hear him, and he perishes – we seek refuge with Allah from the anger of Allah the Exalted.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage describes the tragic state of a person who relies on blind imitation and neglects reflection. It explains how Satan exploits this weakness. When such a person occasionally has a thought about creation, a devil (whether human or jinn) discourages him by claiming that reflection will lead to doubt. So he abandons thinking about death altogether. At the moment of death, when the soul reaches the throat, Satan attacks him in that state of helplessness, planting doubts about his religion, and he dies in a state of doubt. In the grave, his mouth is sealed, and he speaks only what he truly believed. If he was a true knower (arif), he will speak the truth; but if he was a doubter, he will say "I do not know," just as he used to say in his heart during life. The author notes that such a person would experience doubts but would neither investigate them nor cure the sickness of his heart. Consequently, after death he experiences regret and apologizes to one who cannot hear, and he perishes. This is a vivid warning of the consequences of neglecting nazar and allowing doubts to fester.

الشيطان
الشك
الموت
القبر
العارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Occasional doubts are harmless if not acted upon.
Correction: The passage shows that unaddressed doubts lead to death in doubt and eternal regret; one must investigate and cure them.

Checkpoint

A) I believe in Allah
B) I do not know
C) I was wrong
D) I am a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Doubts left uninvestigated lead to a death in doubt and an eternal state of regret and loss.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
