Second Doubt: Change of Nature and Its Refutation
Sanusi presents the second doubt and its Quranic refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second doubt raised against bodily resurrection—that the body's nature changes to dust—and its Quranic refutation using the example of fire from green wood.

Core Idea
God's power over opposites proves resurrection is possible.

This lesson examines the second doubt raised by those who deny bodily resurrection: that the body's nature changes to dust, which seems incompatible with life. Sanusi shows how the Quran refutes this by pointing to the miracle of fire from green wood, demonstrating that God can bring opposites from opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi presents the doubt first, then the Quranic refutation.
The verse is from Surah Ya-Sin.
2
Identify the doubt
The doubt claims that when the body becomes dust, its nature changes from heat and moisture (life) to cold and dryness (dust), making resurrection impossible.
The key term is 'طبع' (nature).
3
Observe the refutation
Sanusi cites the Quranic verse about fire from green wood. Fire is hot and dry, while green wood is cold and moist. This shows God can create opposites from each other.
The verse is a direct response to the doubt.
4
Reflect on the analogy
If God can bring fire from green wood, He can certainly bring life from dust. The analogy undermines the doubt by showing God's power transcends natural properties.
This is a common method in kalam: using God's known acts to argue for what is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شبههم: أنها إذا صارت تراباً فقد تغير طبعها عن طبع الحياة التي هي الحرارة والرطوبة، فرد هذا الاستبعاد بقوله عز وجل: {الَّذِي جَعَلَ لَكُم مِّنَ الشَّجَرِ الْأَخْضَرِ نَارًا} [يس: ٨٠].
Among their doubts: that when it becomes dust, its nature has changed from the nature of life which is heat and moisture, so He refuted this improbability by His statement, mighty and majestic: {He who made for you from the green tree fire} (Ya-Sin 80).
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage presents a second doubt: the body's nature changes to that of dust, characterized by cold and dryness, which seems incompatible with the nature of life (heat and moisture). The Quranic refutation is the verse about producing fire from green wood, which demonstrates that opposite qualities can coexist and that God can bring forth fire (hot and dry) from a green tree (cold and moist). This analogically shows that God can restore life to dust.

Key Terms
طبع
حرارة
رطوبة
استبعاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that a change in physical properties makes resurrection impossible.
Correction: The Quranic example shows that Allah's power transcends natural properties; He can bring life from dust just as He brings fire from green wood.

Key Takeaway

?

?

The First Objection of Deniers Against Resurrection
Sanusi presents two objections of deniers about resurrection and answers the first regarding consumed body parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deniers' argument about consumed body parts and Sanusi's response distinguishing original from accidental parts.

Core Idea
Personal identity in resurrection is preserved through original body parts, regardless of consumption.

Sanusi addresses a classic objection against bodily resurrection: if one person consumes another, how can both be resurrected with the same body? This objection seems to show a contradiction, but Sanusi resolves it by introducing a key distinction between original and accidental parts of the body. This lesson unpacks that argument and its answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Notice it begins with a statement about divine truthfulness, then presents two objections and an answer to the first.
The second objection is mentioned but its answer is not given in this passage.
2
Identify the two objections
The passage lists two proofs (wajhain) from deniers. Find where each starts: the first is about a person eating another, the second about purpose of resurrection.
Only the first objection is answered here.
3
Understand the first objection's logic
The first objection argues that if A eats B, B's parts become part of A. When God resurrects both, those parts cannot be in both bodies simultaneously. This seems to prevent a complete resurrection.
This is a logical puzzle about identity and parts.
4
Examine Sanusi's answer
Sanusi distinguishes between original parts (ajza' asliyya) and accidental parts (ajza' fadliyya) that change with nutrition. Only original parts are essential for personal identity. The eaten parts are accidental and do not determine identity.
Thus, each body maintains its identity through its original parts, and the problem of consumed parts is resolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أن الصادق أخبر بوقوع هذا الممكن: فهذا مما علم من الدين ضرورة. واحتج المنكرون لبعث الأجساد بوجهين: الأول: أن إنساناً لو أكل إنساناً آخر وصار المأكول جزءاً من بدن الآكل؛ فلو أعادهما الله بعينهما: فإما أن تكون الأجزاء المأكولة معادة في بدن المأكول أو في بدن الآكل، وأياً ما كان فلا يكون أحدهما معاداً بعينه وبتمامه، وهو خلاف الفرض، وأيضاً: جعل المأكول جزءاً من بدن أحدهما ليس أولى من جعله جزءاً لبدن الآخر؛ لأنه كان جزءاً لبدن كل واحد منهما قبل العدم في الجملة، ويستحيل جعله جزءاً منهما معاً؛ لاستحالة حلول الشيء الواحد بالشخص في محلين. الوجه الثاني: لو أعيد البدن لم يخل: إما أن يكون لمقصود، أو لا لمقصود، وكلاهما باطل؛ أما الثاني: فإنه يؤدي إلى العبث والسفه، وأما الأول: فإن ذلك المقصود: إما الإيلام، أو تحصيل لذة، أو دفع الألم، والأول لا يصلح أن يكون مقصوداً للحكيم، والثاني باطل؛ لأنه ليس في هذا العالم لذة بالحقيقة، بل كل ذلك خلاص عن ألم، والثالث أيضاً باطل؛ لأنه يحصل بالبقاء على العدم. والجواب عن الأول: أن لكل بدن أجزاء أصلية وأجزاء فضلية (١) التي تتغير بتغير الغذاء فتتزايد بسببه، وتزول وتنقص بسببه.
As for that the truthful informed of the occurrence of this possible: this is something known necessarily from the religion. And the deniers of bodily resurrection argued with two proofs: The first: That if a person ate another person and the eaten became part of the eater's body; then if God were to return them both in their identical forms: either the eaten parts would be returned in the body of the eaten or in the body of the eater, and whichever it is, neither of them would be returned identically and completely, which is contrary to the assumption. Also: making the eaten part of the body of one of them is not more appropriate than making it part of the body of the other; because it was part of the body of each of them before non-existence in general, and it is impossible to make it part of both together because of the impossibility of a single thing with a person subsisting in two places. The second proof: If the body were returned, it would not be free from either being for a purpose or not for a purpose, and both are invalid: As for the second, it leads to futility and foolishness; and as for the first, that purpose is either causing pain, or obtaining pleasure, or repelling pain. The first is not suitable as a purpose for the Wise; the second is invalid because there is in this world no real pleasure, rather all that is relief from pain; and the third is also invalid because it is attained by remaining in non-existence. And the answer to the first: That for every body there are original parts and accidental parts which change with the change of nourishment, so increase because of it, and vanish and decrease because of it.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage begins with a statement that the truthful (the Prophet) informed of the occurrence of this possible matter, and that is known necessarily from religion. Then it presents two objections (wajhain) from deniers of bodily resurrection. The first objection concerns the problem of consumed body parts: if a person eats another, the consumed parts become part of the eater's body. Upon resurrection, these parts cannot be returned to both bodies in their entirety. The second objection argues that resurrection either has a purpose or not, and both are invalid: purposelessness is futile, and any purpose (pain, pleasure, relief) is either unsuitable for a wise God or impossible. The answer to the first objection distinguishes between original and accidental parts of the body; only the original parts are essential for personal identity, and accidental parts that change due to nourishment do not affect identity. The answer to the second objection is not provided in this text.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection about consumed parts refutes the possibility of bodily resurrection entirely.
Correction: Sanusi shows that personal identity is based on original parts, not accidental parts that change with nutrition. Therefore, consumed parts do not hinder resurrection.

Checkpoint
What was the first objection of deniers regarding bodily resurrection?
A) God's power is insufficient
B) Consumed body parts cannot be returned to both bodies identically
C) The body changes nature after death

Key Takeaway
The first objection against resurrection is resolved by distinguishing between original and accidental body parts; only original parts are essential for personal identity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your body has changed dramatically since birth, yet you will be resurrected as the same person. If your identity does not depend on every atom that passes through you, what does it depend on? How does this truth affect your fear of Allah and your hope in His justice on the Day when every soul is judged for what it earned?
?
The deniers thought they found a fatal flaw in resurrection, but Sanusi showed that Allah preserves our original essence. How much of your daily effort goes into building your 'accidental' self—status, wealth, appearance—that will not define you in the grave? What one attachment can you sever today to invest in your eternal identity?
?
Imagine standing before Allah while He reconstructs your original body from the dust. Would you be ashamed of what your accidental parts accumulated—the food of greed, the words of gossip, the steps to sin? What concrete change in your diet of thoughts and actions will you commit to starting right now?

Answer to the First Objection: Eating One Another
Sanusi refutes the first objection against bodily resurrection by distinguishing original from excess parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against bodily resurrection and Sanusi's answer based on the distinction between original and excess parts.

Core Idea
The identity of a body lies in its original parts, not in what it eats.

The denial of bodily resurrection often raises the puzzle of cannibalism: if one person eats another, how can both be resurrected whole? Sanusi presents this objection clearly and then answers it by distinguishing between what is essential to a body and what is merely temporary. This distinction preserves the possibility of bodily resurrection for every human being.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the passage describing the first objection. Notice how it presents a logical dilemma about eaten parts belonging to two bodies.
The objection assumes all parts are equal.
2
Identify Sanusi's distinction
In the answer, Sanusi separates original parts from excess parts. Understand the difference and why it solves the dilemma.
Original parts are permanent; excess parts come and go with nourishment.
3
Apply the distinction
Consider how the resurrected body of each person consists only of his original parts. The eaten parts are excess from the eater, thus not required for the eaten person's resurrection.
This preserves the identity of each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أنَّ الصادق أخبر بوقوع هذا الممكنِ : فهذا ممَّا عُلِمَ مِنَ الدين ضرورة .
واحتج المُنكِرون لبعث الأجساد بوجهين :
الأوّلُ : أَنَّ إنساناً لو أكل إنساناً آخرَ  َوصارَ المأكولُ جزءاً مِنْ بدنِ الآكل ؛ فلو أعادهما الله بعينهما : فإمَّا أنْ تكونَ الأجزاء المأكولةُ مُعادةً في بدنِ المأكول أو في بدنِ الآكل، وأياً ما كانَ فلا يكونُ أحدهما معاداً بعينه وبتمامه ، وهو خلافُ الفَرْضِ ، وأيضاً : جعلُ المأكول جزءاً مِنْ بدنِ أحدهما ليسَ أَولى مِنْ جعله جزءاً لبدنِ الآخرِ ؛ لأنَّهُ كانَ جزءاً لبدن كلّ واحدٍ منهما قبل العدم في الجملة ، ويستحيل جعله جزءاً منهما معاً ؛ لاستحالة حلول الشيء الواحدِ بالشخص في محلَّينِ .
والجواب عنِ الأَوَّلِ : أنَّ لكلِّ بدنِ أجزاء أصليَّةً وأجزاء فضلية(۱)
(۱) التي تتغير بتغير الغذاء فتتزايد بسببه ، وتزول وتنقص بسببه .
« حامدي » وهي ( ص ٤٩٥ ) .
فالمعاد لكل واحدٍ هى أجزاؤُهُ الأصلية ، والمأكولُ فَضْلٌ مِنَ المتغذّي ، فلا يُعادُ فيهِ .
And as for the truthful informing of the occurrence of this possible: this is known from the religion by necessity. And the deniers of bodily resurrection argued with two aspects: The first: That if a person ate another person, and the eaten became part of the body of the eater; then if God returns both as they were, either the eaten parts are returned in the body of the eaten or in the body of the eater, and whichever it is, one of them will not be returned as himself and complete, which is contrary to the assumption. Also, making the eaten a part of one of the bodies is not more appropriate than making it a part of the other, because it was a part of the body of each of them before non-existence in general, and it is impossible to make it a part of both together due to the impossibility of one thing in person residing in two places. The answer to the first: For every body there are original parts and excess parts, which change with food, increase and decrease. So the restored for each is his original parts, and the eaten is excess from the nourished one, so it is not returned in him.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection against bodily resurrection and its answer. The objectors argue: if a person eats another, the eaten parts become part of the eater's body. If God resurrects both identically, those parts can only belong to one body, leaving the other incomplete. Moreover, there is no reason to assign them to one over the other, since they once belonged to both. The answer distinguishes between original parts (ajza' asliyya) and excess parts (ajza' fadliyya). The original parts are permanent and individually restored; the excess parts change with food and are not essential. The eaten parts are excess from the eater's body, so they are not returned in the eaten person's body, preserving his individuality.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection that bodily resurrection is impossible when bodies have intermingled is unanswerable.
Correction: Sanusi shows it is answerable by distinguishing original and excess parts, preserving the possibility of resurrection.

Checkpoint

A) The excess parts
B) The original parts
C) Both original and excess
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Bodily resurrection is possible because each person's identity rests on his original parts, which are restored regardless of bodily changes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your body changes constantly—cells die and are replaced. If your identity depends only on original parts, what does that mean for your sense of self now? How does knowing that God preserves your true physical identity give you hope when you feel lost or changed by life?
?
The eaten person's parts are not returned in him because they became excess in the eater. Does this make you think differently about how God views even the smallest parts of your existence? Are there 'excess' parts of your life you cling to that God may not restore?
?
This objection was meant to disprove resurrection. Instead, it reveals a deeper truth about divine justice. What false beliefs have you held that, when examined, actually lead you closer to the truth? Will you actively seek out and challenge your own doubts?

God's Actions Need No Purpose
Sanusi states the objection and gives the primary refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that God must have a purpose for resurrection is invalid.

Core Idea
God's actions are beyond being motivated by purposes.

The objectors argue that if God restores the body, it must serve a purpose; otherwise it is futile. Sanusi refutes this by stating a fundamental principle: God's actions cannot be explained by purposes or motives. This lesson examines that objection and its primary rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its branches
The objector says the body's return must be either for a purpose or not; both are claimed false. Notice the two branches: futility or a purpose that fails.
2
See why each branch is rejected
The 'no purpose' branch leads to absurdity. The 'purpose' branch splits into three sub-purposes (pain, pleasure, relief from pain), each criticized.
3
Understand the core refutation
Sanusi answers that God's actions cannot be motivated by purposes (ta'leel) at all. This is the key theological principle.
The phrase 'وقد سبق بيانه' refers to earlier discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني : لو أُعيدَ البدنُ لم يخلُ : إِمَّا أَنْ يكونَ لمقصود ، أو لا لمقصود ، وكلاهما باطل ؛ أمَّا الثاني : فلأنَّه يؤدّي إلى العبثِ والسَّفَهِ ، وأَمَّا الأَوَّلُ : فلأنَّ ذلكَ المقصود : إِمَّا الإيلام ، أو تحصيل لذة ، أو دفع الألم ، والأوَّلُ لا يصلح أن يكون مقصوداً للحكيم ، والثاني باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ ليس في هذا العالم لذة بالحقيقة ، بل كلُّ ذلك خلاص عن ألم، والثالثُ أيضاً باطل ؛ لأنَّه يحصل بالبقاء على العدم. والجواب عنِ الثاني : أنَّ أفعالَهُ تعالى يستحيلُ أنْ تُعلَّلَ بالأغراض ، وقد سبق بيانه (۱) ، ولو سُلَّمَ الغرضُ على سبيل الجدل فنقولُ : لِمَ لا يجوز أنْ يكونَ الغرضُ الإلذاذ ؟!
قولهم : ( الاستقراء دلَّ على أنَّ اللذة دفع ألم ( ممنوع ؛ بدليل أنَّ الشيء الملتاً بهِ قد يحصل فجأةً ، فيُلتَلُّ بِهِ مِنْ غيرِ أن يسبق ألمُ الشوقِ إليه ، ولا الشعور بهِ أصلاً ، وعلى تقدير تسليم كونِ اللذة في هذا العالم دفعاً للألم .. فلا نُسلَّمُ أَنَّ لذَاتِ الآخرةِ كذلكَ [ لا اشتراك بينَ لذَّاتِ الدنيا ولذَّاتِ الآخرة إلا في الأسماء ]
فإِنْ قيلَ : قد دلَّ السمعُ على أنَّ لذَّاتِ الآخرةِ مِنْ جنسِ الدنيا ؛ كالأكل والشرب والاستمتاع وغيرها ، فتكون أيضاً دفعاً للألم . فالجواب : أنَّ لذَّاتِ الآخرةِ يشبهُ بعضُها لذَّاتِ الدنيا في الصورة ، ويخالفها في الحقيقةِ ، كما نُقِلَ أَنَّهُ لا شِرْكَةَ بينهما إلا في الأسماءِ (۲) ، وحينئذ لا يلزم اشتراكهما في دفع الألم .
(۱) تقدم ( ص ٥٣٣ ) .
(۲) كما في قوله سبحانه : ﴿ وَأُتُواْ بِهِ مُتَشَبِهَا ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥] .
The second aspect: If the body is returned, it is not free: either it is for a purpose or not for a purpose, and both are false. As for the second: because it leads to futility and foolishness. And as for the first: because that purpose is either causing pain, or achieving pleasure, or repelling pain. The first is not suitable as a purpose for the Wise, the second is false because in this world there is no pleasure in reality, rather all of that is escape from pain, and the third is also false because it can be achieved by remaining in non-existence. The answer to the second: His actions, exalted, are impossible to be motivated by purposes, and its explanation preceded. And if the purpose is granted for the sake of argument, we say: Why is it not permissible that the purpose is pleasure? Their statement: 'Induction indicates that pleasure is repelling pain' is rejected by the evidence that the thing pleasured may occur suddenly, so one takes pleasure in it without preceding pain of longing or any awareness of it. And on the assumption that pleasure in this world is repelling pain, we do not accept that the pleasures of the afterlife are likewise [there is no commonality between the pleasures of this world and the pleasures of the afterlife except in names]. If it is said: Revelation indicates that the pleasures of the afterlife are of the same type as this world, like eating, drinking, and enjoyment, etc., so they would also be repelling pain. The answer: The pleasures of the afterlife resemble some of the pleasures of this world in form, but differ in reality, as it is narrated that there is no commonality between them except in names. In that case, they are not necessarily common in repelling pain.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage refutes the second objection against bodily resurrection. The objectors argue: if God restores the body, it must be for a purpose; otherwise it is futile. If for a purpose, it is either causing pain (unbefitting the Wise), achieving pleasure (but worldly pleasure is only relief from pain), or removing pain (which can be achieved by non-existence). The answer: God's actions cannot be motivated by purposes (ta'leel), as established earlier. Even if we grant purposes for argument, the purpose could be pleasure (iladhdh). The claim that pleasure is only relief from pain is rejected because pleasure can occur suddenly without preceding pain. Moreover, even if worldly pleasure were relief, otherworldly pleasures are fundamentally different, sharing only names. If revelation mentions similar pleasures (eating, drinking), these are mere formal resemblances, not identical in reality, so they need not be relief from pain.

Key Terms
الغرض
العبث
السفه
الإيلام
تحصيل لذة
دفع الألم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's actions must have a purpose or motive like human actions.
Correction: God's actions are not subject to purposes (أغراض); they are free and self-sufficient.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is the second objection (that resurrection must have a purpose) invalid?
A) Because resurrection has no purpose
B) Because God's actions cannot be motivated by purposes
C) Because pleasure is a valid purpose
D) Because the objection contradicts revelation

Key Takeaway
God's actions are beyond being explained by purposes; the objection that resurrection must have a purpose is invalid from the start.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials, do you find yourself demanding that God show you the purpose behind them? How does this lesson challenge your right to demand an explanation from the Creator?
?
Do you ever perform acts of worship expecting a tangible benefit or reward in this world? What does it mean to you that God's actions—including your own existence and trials—are not for external purposes?
?
If God's actions are beyond being motivated by purposes, does that make your worship seem pointless or more about pure love and submission? Honestly, which feeling dominates your heart when you pray?

The Nature of Pleasure: Worldly vs. Otherworldly
Sanusi refutes the claim that pleasure is only relief from pain and distinguishes afterlife pleasures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of the claim that worldly pleasures are merely relief from pain and how otherworldly pleasures are fundamentally different.

Core Idea
Pleasures can be direct, not merely relief, and afterlife pleasures are unique.

Even if we grant that God acts for a purpose, the objectors argue that the purpose must be pleasure — but they claim all pleasure is just relief from pain. Sanusi counters with examples of sudden pleasure and insists that otherworldly pleasures are fundamentally different. This lesson explores that debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the hypothetical grant and the objection about pleasure
Sanusi grants for argument's sake that God acts for a purpose, then asks why that purpose cannot be pleasure. The objector replies that pleasure is merely relief from pain.
This is a dialectical move: accepting the opponent's premise to show it still fails.
2
Examine the counterexample of sudden pleasure
Sanusi rejects the idea that pleasure is always relief by pointing to sudden pleasure that occurs without preceding pain or longing.
Example: unexpectedly seeing something beautiful.
3
Understand the distinction between worldly and otherworldly pleasures
Even if worldly pleasure were relief, Sanusi argues that afterlife pleasures are different in reality, sharing only names.
The phrase 'لا شركة بينهما إلا في الأسماء' is key.
4
See how the objection from revelation is answered
The objector cites verses about eating and drinking in Paradise. Sanusi says these similarities are only in form, not in true nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۱) تقدم ( ص ٥٣٣ ) .
(۲) كما في قوله سبحانه : ﴿ وَأُتُواْ بِهِ مُتَشَبِهَا ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥] .
The second aspect: If the body is returned, it is not free: either it is for a purpose or not for a purpose, and both are false. As for the second: because it leads to futility and foolishness. And as for the first: because that purpose is either causing pain, or achieving pleasure, or repelling pain. The first is not suitable as a purpose for the Wise, the second is false because in this world there is no pleasure in reality, rather all of that is escape from pain, and the third is also false because it can be achieved by remaining in non-existence. And if the purpose is granted for the sake of argument, we say: Why is it not permissible that the purpose is pleasure? Their statement: 'Induction indicates that pleasure is repelling pain' is rejected by the evidence that the thing pleasured may occur suddenly, so one takes pleasure in it without preceding pain of longing or any awareness of it. And on the assumption that pleasure in this world is repelling pain, we do not accept that the pleasures of the afterlife are likewise [there is no commonality between the pleasures of this world and the pleasures of the afterlife except in names]. If it is said: Revelation indicates that the pleasures of the afterlife are of the same type as this world, like eating, drinking, and enjoyment, etc., so they would also be repelling pain. The answer: The pleasures of the afterlife resemble some of the pleasures of this world in form, but differ in reality, as it is narrated that there is no commonality between them except in names. In that case, they are not necessarily common in repelling pain.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage refutes the second objection against bodily resurrection. The objectors argue: if God restores the body, it must be for a purpose; otherwise it is futile. If for a purpose, it is either causing pain (unbefitting the Wise), achieving pleasure (but worldly pleasure is only relief from pain), or removing pain (which can be achieved by non-existence). The answer: God's actions cannot be motivated by purposes (ta'leel), as established earlier. Even if we grant purposes for argument, the purpose could be pleasure (iladhdh). The claim that pleasure is only relief from pain is rejected because pleasure can occur suddenly without preceding pain. Moreover, even if worldly pleasure were relief, otherworldly pleasures are fundamentally different, sharing only names. If revelation mentions similar pleasures (eating, drinking), these are mere formal resemblances, not identical in reality, so they need not be relief from pain.

Key Terms
الإلذاذ
الاستقراء
دفع الألم
لذات الآخرة
تشابه الأسماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All pleasure is merely relief from pain, and afterlife pleasures are identical to worldly ones.
Correction: Pleasure can be sudden and independent of pain; afterlife pleasures are unique in reality, only similar in name.

Checkpoint
What example does Sanusi give to refute the claim that pleasure is always relief from pain?
A) The pleasure of eating after hunger
B) Sudden pleasure without preceding pain
C) The pleasure of the afterlife
D) The pleasure of knowledge

Key Takeaway
Pleasure is not always relief from pain, and afterlife pleasures are fundamentally different from worldly ones, so they can serve as a genuine purpose for resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson challenges the idea that pleasure must always come after pain. When you experience a sudden joy or blessing from Allah, do you recognize it as a direct gift, or do you assume it was earned by some prior hardship? How can you train yourself to see every pleasure as a direct act of divine generosity?
?
If Paradise's pleasures are fundamentally different from worldly ones, how does that change the way you long for them? Are you still attached to the limited pleasures of this world as if they are the ultimate good? What concrete step can you take today to shift your desire toward the unique, genuine pleasures of the afterlife?
?
Sanusi argues that even the descriptions of Paradise (eating, drinking) are only similar in form, not reality. Does this make you question the reliability of those descriptions? Or does it deepen your trust that Allah's promise is beyond imagination? How will you respond when worldly pleasures fail to satisfy—will you turn to the promise of something truly different and better?

The Sirat: A Real Bridge Over Hell
Sanusi defines the Sirat and refutes Mu'tazila metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sirat is a real physical bridge in the afterlife and why the Mu'tazila's metaphorical interpretation is rejected.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge; the Mu'tazila wrongly interpret it metaphorically.

This lesson examines Sanusi's definition of the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). He affirms it as a real, physical structure that all people will cross, based on transmitted reports. He then refutes the Mu'tazila who interpret it symbolically, arguing that God's power makes such a bridge possible without doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of the Sirat
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the basic claim: it is a bridge stretched over Hell.
Notice the word 'جسر' (bridge) – it affirms a physical structure.
2
Note the hadith about fineness
The passage mentions it is finer than a hair; consider what this implies about its reality.
This hadith reinforces the literal nature of the Sirat.
3
Understand the speed according to deeds
People cross at speeds based on their deeds, tying resurrection to moral accountability.
This shows the Sirat is a test of faith and works.
4
Follow the argument from divine power
God who holds the heavens and earth can make people walk on such a bridge; this removes rational doubt.
Sanusi uses a rational argument to support literal interpretation.
5
Recognize the refutation of Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila interpret it figuratively; Sanusi rejects this as opposite to the apparent meaning.
The Mu'tazila are criticized for departing from the literal sense of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الصراط : فهو جسر ممدود على متْنِ جَهَنَّمَ يَرِدُهُ الأَوَّلُونَ والآخرون ، ووردَ : أَنَّهُ أدقُ مِنَ الشعرة (٢) ، وتكون سرعة الناس عليه على قدْرِ أعمالهم ، ومَنْ أمسكَ السماوات والأرضِ أنْ تزولا .. قادر أنْ يُسيَّرَ العباد معتمدين على شيءٍ وعلى غيرِ شيء ، فلا معنى لتلجلج الشكّ في ثبوتِهِ أَوِ التعرُّض لتأويلِهِ على خلاف الظاهرِ كما سلكته المعتزلة (۳)
As for the Ṣirāṭ: it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Jahannam, which the first and the last will come to. And it has been reported that it is finer than a hair (2). The speed of people upon it is according to their deeds. And the One who holds the heavens and the earth from ceasing to exist is able to cause the servants to walk relying on something and on nothing. So there is no meaning for the agitation of doubt concerning its establishment or the attempt to interpret it contrary to the apparent meaning, as the Mu‘tazila have done (3).
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the Ṣirāṭ (the bridge). The author begins by defining the Ṣirāṭ as a real bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, which all people will approach. He then mentions a transmitted report (al-ḥadīth) that it is finer than a hair, and that people cross it at speeds proportional to their deeds. The author argues that the same God who holds the heavens and earth from collapse is able to make people walk on such a bridge, relying on something or on nothing—so there is no rational basis for doubt about its reality. Finally, he criticizes the Mu‘tazila for interpreting the Ṣirāṭ metaphorically, contrary to its apparent meaning. The footnote markers likely refer to the hadith and to the Mu‘tazila position.

Key Terms
الصراط (al-Ṣirāṭ)
الجسر (al-jisr)
جهنم (Jahannam)
المعتزلة (al-Mu‘tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe the Sirat is merely metaphorical and not a physical bridge.
Correction: Sanusi insists it is a real bridge, supported by hadith and rational argument from God's power.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the Ṣirāṭ and how do the Mu‘tazila err regarding it?
A) The Ṣirāṭ is a metaphorical path; the Mu‘tazila rightly interpret it.
B) The Ṣirāṭ is a real bridge; the Mu‘tazila wrongly interpret it figuratively.
C) The Ṣirāṭ is not mentioned in revelation; it is a philosophical concept.
D) The Ṣirāṭ is a spiritual state; the Mu‘tazila deny it.

Key Takeaway
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell that all people must cross, and its reality is confirmed by revelation and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were standing at the edge of the Sirat right now, knowing that your deeds alone determine your speed, what single action in your life would you most urgently want to change before stepping onto it?
?
Sanusi says there is no room for doubt about the Sirat's reality. Where in your heart do you still treat the afterlife as less real than your daily routines? What will you do today to narrow that gap?
?
The One who holds the heavens and the earth can make you walk on nothing. Does your trust in Allah's power over the unseen match your trust in what you can see? Name one fear you will surrender to Him this week because of this lesson.

The Reality and Description of the Balance
Sanusi affirms the Balance and describes its components and contents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Balance is a real physical scale with a column and two pans, and that deeds are weighed in the form of scrolls or exemplars created by Allah.

Core Idea
The Balance is a real scale, not a metaphor.

Sanusi begins by affirming the reality of the Balance (Mīzān) as an article of faith derived from the Qur'an and Sunnah. He describes its physical form according to Ahl al-Sunnah and specifies what is weighed. This lesson establishes the basic Sunni doctrine of the Balance.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmation
Read the first sentence where Sanusi states that the Balance is true and proven by revelation. Note the source of authority: Qur'an and Sunnah.
2
Identify the physical description
Find the part describing the Balance as having a column (عمود) and two pans (كفتين). This is the Sunni position.
3
Understand what is weighed
Notice the two views: either scrolls of deeds (صحف الأعمال) or exemplars (مثالات) created by Allah. The weighing is according to the value of deeds.
These are not contradictory but complementary explanations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا الميزانُ : فهو حق ، وردَ بهِ القرآنُ والسنَّةُ ، وهو بعمود وكفتين عند أهل السنَّةِ ، والموزون فيه : صحفُ الأعمال ، أو مثالات يخلقها الله تعالى ويَزِنُها الله جل وعلا على قدر أجور الأعمال وما يتعلق بها مِنْ ثوابها وعقابها
وأنكر معظمُ المعتزلة ذلكَ ، وأوَّلوا الوزن على اعتبار الحسناتِ ، وقالوا : وزَنُ كلِّ شيءٍ بما يليقُ بهِ ، وقالَ ابنُ المعتمر منهم : يجوزُ ، ولا يُقطَعُ به سمعا (٤) ، ولا يخفى بطلان القولين .
وقال الجبائي : يخلقُ الله تعالى جواهر على أعداد الأعمال الصالحة وضدها
قيل : وما ذكرَهُ غيرُ بعيد ، إلا أنَّهُ وردَ : أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاة والسلام سُئِلَ عن ذلك ، فقال : « تُوزَنُ الصُّحُفُ (١)
وهل الوزنُ خاص بالمؤمنينَ ، أو عام لهم وللكافرين ، ويكون معنى قوله تعالى : ( فَلَا تُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَمَةِ وَزَنَا أي : نافعاً ؟ فيه تردد .
As for the Mīzān: it is true, affirmed by the Qur’an and Sunnah. It has a column and two pans according to Ahl al-Sunnah. What is weighed in it are the scrolls of deeds, or exemplars that Allah creates and Allah weighs according to the worth of deeds and what pertains to them of reward and punishment. Most of the Mu‘tazila denied that and interpreted weighing as considering good deeds, saying: the weighing of each thing is in a manner befitting it. Ibn al-Mu‘tamir among them said: it is possible, but it is not decisively established by revelation (4). The falsehood of both statements is not hidden. Al-Jubbā’ī said: Allah creates jewels in the number of righteous deeds and their opposite. It was said: what he mentioned is not far-fetched, except that it has been reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about that and said: 'The scrolls are weighed' (1). And is the weighing specific to the believers, or general for them and the disbelievers, such that the meaning of His saying: “So We shall not establish for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight” (18:105) is 'any beneficial weight'? There is hesitation about that.
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the Mīzān (the Balance). The author first asserts its reality as proven by Qur’an and Sunnah, then describes it according to Ahl al-Sunnah as having a column and two pans. He specifies that what is weighed are either the scrolls of deeds or exemplars created by Allah, which are weighed in proportion to the worth of deeds and their resulting reward or punishment. The author then reports that most Mu‘tazila denied this, interpreting weighing as merely considering good deeds, and that Ibn al-Mu‘tamir allowed it intellectually but said it is not decisively proven from revelation. The author dismisses both views as clearly false. He then mentions al-Jubbā’ī’s view that Allah creates jewels corresponding to deeds, and notes that while this is not far-fetched, a hadith reports that the scrolls themselves are weighed. Finally, the author raises a question: whether the weighing applies only to believers or to both believers and disbelievers, referencing the verse that says 'no weight' will be established for disbelievers—possibly meaning no beneficial weight. He notes hesitation on this point.

Key Terms
الميزان
العمود
الكفتين
صحف الأعمال
المثالات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance is merely a metaphor for divine justice, not a physical object.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states it has a column and two pans, indicating a real physical scale. This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the Balance have according to Ahl al-Sunnah?
A) A beam and a single pan
B) A column and two pans
C) Two columns and one pan
D) No physical parts, only symbolic

Key Takeaway
The Balance is a real scale with a column and two pans, weighing scrolls or exemplars of deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your deeds were weighed today, would the scale tip toward reward or punishment? What specific action from this past week would you most fear being on the lighter side?
?
The Balance has two pans—one for reward, one for punishment. Are you living in a way that intentionally fills the reward pan? What have you done today that you hope will add weight to it?
?
You believe the Balance is real. Does that belief change how you treat a family member or coworker when no one is watching? Give a concrete example from your life where that belief could (or should) have made a difference.

Refuting Mu'tazila Denials of the Balance
Sanusi reports and refutes Mu'tazila views on the Balance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila denial of a physical balance, their alternative interpretations, and the Sunni refutation based on the hadith of weighing scrolls.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila denial of a physical balance is false; the Prophet confirmed the weighing of scrolls.

Sanusi now addresses those who reject a literal Balance. He reports the views of most Mu'tazila, including Ibn al-Mu'tamir and al-Jubbā'ī, and then dismisses them as false. He also cites a hadith where the Prophet explicitly says scrolls are weighed, settling the matter for Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila position
Identify that most Mu'tazila denied the physical Balance and reinterpreted weighing as 'considering good deeds.' Note their claim that each thing is weighed in a manner befitting it.
2
Note Ibn al-Mu'tamir's concession
Ibn al-Mu'tamir allowed the possibility but said it is not decisively proven by revelation. Sanusi calls both views false.
3
Examine al-Jubbā'ī's alternative
Al-Jubbā'ī proposed that Allah creates jewels equal in number to deeds. Sanusi notes this is not far-fetched but then presents the hadith that overrides it.
4
Learn the conclusive hadith
The Prophet was asked about weighing and said, 'The scrolls are weighed.' This shows that the actual scrolls are weighed, not just metaphors or jewels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا الميزانُ : فهو حق ، وردَ بهِ القرآنُ والسنَّةُ ، وهو بعمود وكفتين عند أهل السنَّةِ ، والموزون فيه : صحفُ الأعمال ، أو مثالات يخلقها الله تعالى ويَزِنُها الله جل وعلا على قدر أجور الأعمال وما يتعلق بها مِنْ ثوابها وعقابها

?

Are there any commands or descriptions of the afterlife that you avoid taking literally because they feel too 'physical' or uncomfortable? What does that avoidance reveal about the state of your submission to revelation?
?

Where in your own life do you prefer intellectual speculation over submitting to the plain meaning of the Prophet's teachings? Will you commit to accepting the hadith as it comes, even when your intellect protests?

The Scope of Weighing: Believers vs Disbelievers
Sanusi raises a question about the scope of weighing and cites a verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly hesitation about whether the weighing on the Day of Judgment applies to both believers and disbelievers, and the interpretation of the verse 'no weight' as meaning no beneficial weight.

Core Idea
The weighing may be general, but for disbelievers it is not beneficial.

Sanusi concludes with a nuanced question: is the weighing specific to believers, or does it include disbelievers as well? He references the Qur'anic verse that says 'no weight' will be established for disbelievers, and suggests that this may mean no beneficial weight. The existence of this hesitation shows the depth of scholarly reflection on the matter.

Guided Path
1
Understand the question
Read the question posed by Sanusi: Is the weighing specific to believers or general for both believers and disbelievers?
2
Consider the verse
The verse 'So We shall not establish for them any weight' (18:105) is interpreted as meaning no beneficial weight. This suggests that disbelievers are weighed but their weight is worthless.
3
Note the hesitation
Sanusi says there is 'hesitation' (تردد) about this, meaning there is no single definitive position among scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The author dismisses both views as clearly false. Finally, the author raises a question: whether the weighing applies only to believers or to both believers and disbelievers, referencing the verse that says 'no weight' will be established for disbelievers—possibly meaning no beneficial weight. He notes hesitation on this point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
There is scholarly hesitation about whether the weighing includes disbelievers, but the verse likely means no beneficial weight for them.

Al-Jubba'i's Theory and the Hadith of Scrolls
Examination of al-Jubba'i's theory and prophetic alternative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Jubba'i's rationalist theory of weighing deeds and the prophetic response affirming the weighing of scrolls.

Core Idea
The Prophet corrected al-Jubba'i's theory by revealing that scrolls, not jewels, are weighed.

Al-Jubba'i proposed a speculative theory about the weighing of deeds, suggesting Allah creates jewels to represent each deed. However, the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about this and gave a different answer: the scrolls are weighed. This lesson examines that exchange and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Jubba'i's opinion is presented first, then countered with a hadith.
2
Understand al-Jubba'i's view
Identify what al-Jubba'i claimed: that Allah creates jewels corresponding to every good and bad deed. Consider why this might be seen as rational.
Al-Jubba'i was a Mu'tazilite scholar known for rationalist theology.
3
Note the prophetic response
The Prophet said 'The scrolls are weighed.' Contrast this with al-Jubba'i's jewels. What does 'scrolls' imply about the recording of deeds?
The hadith suggests that deeds themselves are recorded in scrolls and those are weighed.
4
Reflect on the author's stance
The author says al-Jubba'i's view is 'not far-fetched' but then presents the hadith. Why might he not outright reject al-Jubba'i?
The author may be acknowledging that rational speculation is not wrong, but revelation takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الجبائي : يخلق الله تعالى جواهر على أعداد الأعمال الصالحة وضدها . قيل : وما ذكره غير بعيد ، إلا أنه ورد : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام سئل عن ذلك ، فقال : « توزن الصحف » . وهل الوزن خاص بالمؤمنين ، أو عام لهم وللكافرين ، ويكون معنى قوله تعالى : ( فلا نقيم لهم يوم القيامة وزنا ) أي : نافعا ؟ فيه تردد .
Al-Jubba'i said: Allah creates jewels according to the numbers of righteous deeds and their opposites. It was said: What he mentioned is not far-fetched, except that it is reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about that and said: 'The scrolls are weighed.' And is the weighing specific to the believers, or general to them and to the disbelievers? And is the meaning of His saying (So We shall not set up for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight) i.e., beneficial? There is hesitation regarding it.
Source pages p. 618

Commentary
This passage discusses the weighing of deeds (wazn al-a'mal) on the Day of Judgment. It begins by mentioning the opinion of al-Jubba'i, a Mu'tazilite scholar, who held that Allah creates jewels (jawahir) that correspond to each good and bad deed, presumably to facilitate the weighing. The author says this opinion is not far-fetched, but then notes that there is a hadith about the weighing of scrolls (suhuf). The author then raises a question about the scope of the weighing: is it specifically for believers, or does it include disbelievers as well? The author cites the verse (18:105) which says that on the Day of Resurrection, We shall not assign any weight (wazn) to the deeds of disbelievers. The author interprets 'weight' here as beneficial weight. The passage concludes that there is hesitation (taraddud) on this point, meaning the issue is not settled definitively.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Jubba'i's opinion is rejected outright as false.
Correction: The author says it is not far-fetched, but the hadith provides the definitive answer.

Questioning the scope of weighing and interpreting a Quranic verse

Creation of Paradise and Hell: Refuting the Mu'tazilite Denial
Affirms creation of Paradise and Hell and refutes Mu'tazilite denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine that Paradise and Hell are already created, and the refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that they are not yet created.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are created now, not just in the future.

This lesson addresses a key point in Islamic eschatology: whether Paradise and Hell are already created. The author affirms that their existence is known by necessity and provides scriptural and rational proofs, while refuting the Mu'tazilite reinterpretation. The passage also demonstrates the correct approach to divine attributes and actions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the affirmative claim
Read the author's opening statement that Paradise and Hell are created and known by necessity. Note the three proofs provided.
The proofs include a Quranic verse, the descent of Adam, and the Prophet's Night Journey.
2
Examine the Mu'tazilite objection
Identify the Mu'tazilite arguments: no benefit before Judgment Day, and their reinterpretation of 'Prepared' and the Paradise of Adam.
The author calls this reinterpretation 'tampering with religion.'
3
Reflect on the refutation
The author argues that God's actions are not dependent on purposes, and even if they were, hidden benefits exist such as strengthening faith and benefiting inhabitants.
Consider how this refutation defends the traditional understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجنة والنار : فثبوتهما مما علم من الدين ضرورة ، وهما مخلوقتان ؛ بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿ أعدت للمتقين ﴾ [آل عمران : 133] ، وهبوط آدم منها ، ورؤية النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لهما في الإسراء وفي غيره . وقد أنكر جماعة من المعتزلة خلقهما ، وزعموا : أنه لا فائدة في خلقهما قبل الثواب والعقاب ، وحملوا ( أعدت ) على أنه من باب التعبير عن المستقبل بالماضي لتحقق وقوعه ، وحملوا ( الجنة ) في قصة آدم عليه السلام على بستان من بساتين الأرض ، وهذا تلاعب بالدين . وأفعال الله تعالى لا تتوقف على الأغراض ، بل يفعل ما يشاء ، ويحكم ما يريد . ولو تنزلنا معهم في إيقافها على الأغراض.. فما المانع من اشتمالها على فائدة عجزت عقولنا عن الوقوف عليها ؟! أو نقول : ما المانع أن يكون في إعدادها لطف في الإيمان بإكمال تحقيق الوعد والوعيد ، ونفع من كان بها من الحور والولدان ومن يرد عليهم من أرواح الشهداء والأولياء والأطفال ، وكذا أرواح الكفار بالنسبة إلى النار ؟!
As for Paradise and Hellfire, their existence is known from religion by necessity, and they are created; evidence includes His saying: (Prepared for the righteous) [3:133], and the descent of Adam from it, and the Prophet's seeing them in the Night Journey and elsewhere. A group of the Mu'tazilites denied their creation, claiming that there is no benefit in creating them before reward and punishment. They interpreted (Prepared) as being from the category of expressing the future with the past due to its certain occurrence, and they interpreted (Paradise) in the story of Adam as a garden of the earthly gardens. This is tampering with religion. The actions of Allah do not depend on purposes; rather, He does what He wills and judges what He desires. If we were to concede with them regarding their dependence on purposes, then what prevents them from containing a benefit that our minds fail to comprehend? Or we say: what prevents that their preparation is an act of grace in faith by completing the fulfillment of the promise and threat, and benefiting those who are there from the houris and boys and those who visit them from the souls of martyrs, saints, and children, as well as the souls of disbelievers with respect to the Fire?
Source pages p. 618

Commentary
This passage affirms the creation of Paradise and Hell and refutes the Mu'tazilite denial. The author begins by stating that their existence is known from religion by necessity (darurah), and they are created (makhluqatan). Three proofs are given: the verse 'Prepared for the righteous' (3:133), the descent of Adam from Paradise, and the Prophet seeing both in the Night Journey and elsewhere. Then the author mentions that some Mu'tazilites denied their creation, arguing no benefit before the Day of Judgment. They reinterpreted 'Prepared' as a future event described in past tense for certainty, and interpreted the Paradise of Adam as an earthly garden. The author calls this tampering with religion. The refutation continues: God's actions are not contingent on purposes (aghrâḍ). If we hypothetically accept that they are contingent, then why cannot there be a hidden benefit? The author proposes several possibilities: the preparation is an act of grace (luṭf) to strengthen faith by fulfilling the promise and threat, and it benefits the inhabitants (houris, boys, souls of martyrs, saints, children, and even disbelievers' souls in the Fire).

الجنة
النار
مخلوقتان
المعتزلة
أعدت
هبوط آدم
لطف
وعد
وعيد
حور
ولدان
شهداء
أولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell are not yet created; they will be created only after the Day of Judgment.
Correction: Paradise and Hell are already created, as evidenced by the Quran, the descent of Adam, and the Prophet's visions. Denying this is tampering with religion.

Checkpoint

A) They misinterpret the Quran and ignore clear proofs
B) They rely on reason over revelation
C) They deny the possibility of benefit
D) They follow a different school

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are created now, as affirmed by scripture and reason, and the Mu'tazilite denial is a form of tampering with religion.

The Objection that Created Paradise Would Perish and the Response
The Mu'tazilite objection that created Paradise would perish, and the Sunni response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars respond to the Mu'tazilite objection that if Paradise and Hell are created, they would perish, using the principle of specification (takhṣīṣ) and the timing of the Hereafter.

Core Idea
The verse 'Everything perishes' is general but specified to exclude the eternal bliss of Paradise.

This lesson presents a key objection from the Mu'tazilites against the Sunni belief that Paradise and Hell are created. They argue that if these abodes were created, they would be subject to annihilation, contradicting verses that promise eternal bliss. The response clarifies how the Qur'anic statement about perishing is not absolute but specified, and how the timing of the Hereafter resolves the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the Mu'tazilite argument using the two verses: one promises eternal bliss, the other says everything perishes. See the apparent contradiction.
The objection assumes that if Paradise is created, it must perish like all created things.
2
Examine the first response
The first response says the perishing applies before entering the Hereafter, not after. This resolves the timing conflict.
The verse 'Everything is perishing' refers to the state before the final judgment.
3
Examine the second response
The second response says the verse 'Everything is perishing' is general (ʿāmm) but specified (makṣūṣ) to exclude the abode of the Hereafter.
Specification (takhṣīṣ) is a key principle in Islamic jurisprudence and theology.
4
Connect to the broader theology
This shows how Muslims reconcile apparently conflicting texts using tools like specification and contextual interpretation.
The belief that Paradise and Hell are created and eternal is upheld.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجوا : بأنهما لو كانتا مخلوقتين لوجب ألا ينقطع نعيم الجنة ؛ لقول تعالى : ( أكلها دائم وظلها ) [الرعد : 35] ، وقد قال تعالى : ( كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه ) [القصص : 88] . والجواب : أن ذلك بعد دخولهما في الآخرة ، أو نقول : قوله تعالى : ( كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه ) عام مخصوص .
They argued: If they were created, then the bliss of Paradise must inevitably cease, because of His saying: (Its fruit is eternal and its shade) [13:35], and He said: (Everything is perishing except His Face) [28:88]. The answer: That is after they enter the Hereafter, or we say: His saying (Everything is perishing except His Face) is general but specified.
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from the Mu'tazilites and the Sunni response. The objection is: if Paradise and Hell are created, then their bliss must end, because of two verses: one states that the fruit and shade of Paradise are eternal (13:35), implying permanence, but another says everything will perish except God's Face (28:88). This seems contradictory if Paradise is created. The answer is twofold. First, the cessation of blessings applies only after the final judgment, before entry into the Hereafter. Second, the verse 'Everything is perishing' is general (ʿāmm) but specified (makṣūṣ) to exclude the abode of the Hereafter. Thus, Paradise and Hell are created and will endure after the resurrection.

Key Terms
نعيم الجنة
كل شيء هالك
عام مخصوص
الآخرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse 'Everything is perishing' (28:88) contradicts the possibility of created things being eternal, so Paradise cannot be both created and eternal.
Correction: The verse is general but specified to exclude the Hereafter, and the perishing applies before the final judgment, not after.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the Mu'tazilite claim that if Paradise were created, its blessings would cease?
A) By denying the verse about perishing
B) By saying the verse applies only to this world
C) By saying the verse is general but specified for the Hereafter
D) By saying Paradise is not created

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Everything is perishing' is general but specified to exclude the Hereafter, so Paradise and Hell can be created and eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'Everything perishes except His Face', does a subtle doubt ever creep into your heart about whether your ultimate hope for eternal bliss is secure? How will you actively remind yourself of the specification in this verse the next time that doubt arises?
?
You have just learned that Paradise is created yet eternal. If that is truly your eternal home, what one worldly attachment are you still clinging to that you must release today to live in light of that reality?
?
The Mu'tazilites rejected the eternity of Paradise because of a misapplied verse. Are there any verses or hadith you have unconsciously misinterpreted to avoid a difficult command or to justify a comfortable sin? What step will you take this week to correct that interpretation?

The Punishment of the Grave: Quranic Proof
The author affirms the punishment of the grave and its proof from the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave is a core Sunni doctrine supported by explicit Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The Quran itself affirms punishment in the grave for the wicked and bliss for the blessed.

Sanusi now turns to a topic from the samʿiyyāt: the punishment of the grave. This doctrine is often questioned, but the author shows it is firmly rooted in the Quran. In this passage, he presents two key verses that establish the reality of the grave experience for both the righteous and the wicked.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the author's concise statement. Note the structure: a general claim then two specific proofs.
The passage is short but packed with doctrine.
2
Identify the two groups
The proof is divided for the blessed (saʿadāʾ) and the wicked (ashqiyāʾ). Notice how each group has its own verse.
3
Examine the verses
Reflect on how each verse indicates an intermediate state after death—for martyrs (3:169) and for Pharaoh's people (40:46).
These verses are not about the Day of Judgment but about a current state.
4
Connect to doctrine
Understand that these verses are the basis for the Sunni belief in ʿadhāb al-qabr (punishment of the grave).
This is a samʿiyyāt matter, accepted based on revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عذاب القبر وإحياء الميت فيه وسؤاله : فهو حق عند جميع أهل السنة ، ودليله : القرآن الكريم . أما في حق السعداء : فقوله تعالى : ( ولا تحسبن الذين قتلوا في سبيل الله أمواتا بل أحياء عند ربهم يرزقون ) [آل عمران : 169] . وأما في حق الأشقياء : فقوله تعالى : ( النار يعرضون عليها غدوا وعشيا ) [غافر : 46] .
As for the punishment of the grave and the reviving of the dead therein and his questioning: it is true according to all Ahl al-Sunnah, and its proof is the Noble Qur'an. With respect to the blessed, His saying: (And do not think that those who are killed in the path of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord being provided) [3:169]. And with respect to the wicked, His saying: (The Fire: they are exposed to it morning and evening) [40:46].
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage affirms the doctrine of the punishment of the grave (ʿadhāb al-qabr). The author states that it is a truth (ḥaqq) according to all Ahl al-Sunnah. Its proof is the Quran. For the blessed (saʿadāʾ), the author cites the verse about martyrs who are killed in God's path: they are not dead but alive and provided for (3:169). For the wicked (ashqiyāʾ), the author cites the verse about Pharaoh's people who are exposed to the Fire morning and evening (40:46). These verses indicate that the soul experiences bliss or torment before the Day of Judgment, which is the basis for the punishment of the grave.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
إحياء الميت
سؤال
أهل السنة
سعداء
أشقياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The punishment of the grave is not mentioned in the Quran and was invented later.
Correction: The author shows that the Quran explicitly mentions the state of souls after death for both the blessed and the wicked, which forms the basis for the doctrine.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the Quranic proof for the punishment of the grave for the wicked?
A) The verse about martyrs being alive
B) The verse about Paradise being prepared
C) The verse about the Fire being shown morning and evening
D) The verse about the scales

Key Takeaway
The Quran provides explicit evidence for the punishment of the grave, proving that souls experience reward or punishment immediately after death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight, which verse—3:169 or 40:46—would describe the state of your soul? Why? What in your life right now confirms that?
?
The Quran explicitly states that the wicked are exposed to the Fire 'morning and evening' before judgment. Have you ever allowed yourself to ignore this reality when making choices? What one habit will you change today to take this seriously?
?
Martyrs are described as 'alive' and 'provided for' immediately after death. Does your current level of faith and sacrifice reflect a longing for that state? What is holding you back from living as if you will meet your Lord tonight?

The Scriptural Proof for the Punishment of the Grave
Sanusi presents Quranic verses and hadith as evidence for the punishment of the grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic and hadith evidence that establishes the reality of the punishment of the grave as an intermediate state between death and the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Quran and Sunnah confirm an intermediate punishment before the Final Judgment.

This lesson examines the specific scriptural proofs that the punishment of the grave is a real intermediate state. Sanusi cites two Quranic verses and a well-known hadith, showing how these texts cannot be interpreted as referring only to the Hereafter. He also notes the continuous practice of the early community in acknowledging this reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here, weaving together multiple proofs.
2
Identify the two Quranic arguments
The passage presents two Quranic verses. Identify each verse and how Sanusi uses it to prove an intermediate punishment distinct from the Hereafter.
Pay attention to the word 'فَ' in the second verse, indicating immediate sequence.
3
Understand the hadith and Salaf practice
The passage then cites a hadith and notes its widespread transmission. Consider how this hadith complements the Quranic evidence, and note the mention of the Salaf's practice.
This shows that the belief in punishment of the grave was not an innovation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَشِيَّا [غافر : ٤٦] ، ولا يصح أن يكون المراد منه عذابَ الآخرةِ ؛ لعدم تقيده بالغدو والعشي (۱) ، ولقوله تعالى : ﴿وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ (۲) أَدْخِلُوا وَالَ فِرْعَوْنَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَابِ ﴾ [غافر : ٤٦] ، فميَّر بين العذابين وقوله تعالى : ﴿ أَغْرِقُوا فَأُدْخِلُوا نَارًا ﴾ [نوح : ٢٥] ، والفاء للترتيب باتصال . ووردَتْ أخبار بالغةٌ حدَّ الاستفاضة باستعادتِهِ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنْ عذاب القبرِ ، وقالَ : « الْقَبْرُ رَوْضَةٌ مِنْ رِيَاضِ الْجَنَّةِ ، أَوْ حُفْرَةٌ مِنْ حُفَرِ النَّارِ (۳) ، ثم لم يزل ذلكَ مستفيضاً بينَ السلف قبل ظهورِ البدع .
And 'evening' [Quran 40:46], and it is not correct that the intended meaning is the punishment of the Hereafter because it is not restricted to morning and evening, and because of His statement: 'And on the Day the Hour establishes, enter the family of Pharaoh into the severest punishment' [Quran 40:46], so He distinguished between the two punishments; and His statement: 'They were drowned and then made to enter a Fire' [Quran 71:25], and the fa (ف) indicates immediate sequence. And there have come reports reaching the level of widespread transmission (istifāḍah) that he (peace and blessings be upon him) sought refuge from the punishment of the grave, and he said: 'The grave is a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' Then this continued to be widespread among the Salaf before the emergence of innovations.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage presents the scriptural proof for the punishment of the grave. The author begins by citing Quran 40:46, which mentions that they are exposed to the fire morning and evening. He argues that this cannot refer to the punishment of the Hereafter because that punishment is eternal and not restricted to specific times. Then he cites another part of the same verse that distinguishes between two punishments. He also cites Quran 71:25, where the conjunction 'fa' indicates immediate sequence, implying an intermediate punishment. Then he cites hadiths, including the Prophet seeking refuge from punishment of the grave and his statement describing the grave as a garden or pit. He concludes that these reports were widespread among the Salaf before the emergence of innovations.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
استفاضة
سلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse in Surah Ghafir (40:46) refers to the eternal punishment of the Hereafter.
Correction: Sanusi argues that because the punishment is qualified by morning and evening, it must be an intermediate state before the Day of Judgment, as the eternal punishment is not time-bound.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi argue that the verse 'exposed to the fire morning and evening' cannot refer to the punishment of the Hereafter?
A) Because the Hereafter punishment is eternal and not time-bound
B) Because the verse mentions both morning and evening separately
C) Because the verse is about Pharaoh's family only
D) Because the Prophet said the grave is a garden

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is established by clear Quranic and Prophetic statements, and was consistently affirmed by the early Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The grave is either a garden or a pit based on your deeds. What specific action will you take today to ensure it becomes a garden, and how will you hold yourself accountable for it tonight?
?
The Prophet himself sought refuge from the punishment of the grave. When was the last time you sincerely recited that supplication and meant it? If you haven't, what is stopping you from making it a daily habit starting now?
?
The Salaf held this belief before innovations arose. Are there any beliefs about the afterlife that you have taken lightly or ignored, thinking they are not essential? How will you change that starting this week?

The Complete Denial of the Punishment of the Grave
Sanusi reports the absolute denial of grave punishment by Ḍirār, Bishr al-Marīsī, and their group.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme Mu'tazilī position of Ḍirār and Bishr al-Marīsī that completely denies the punishment of the grave, the questioning, and the return of souls.

Core Idea
Some Mu'tazila rejected the punishment of the grave entirely.

Sanusi begins his survey of erroneous views by citing the most radical denial: that of Ḍirār, Bishr al-Marīsī, and their followers. They rejected not only the punishment but also the questioning and the return of souls to bodies in the grave. This lesson examines their stance and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation of the passage to understand the position being described.
The passage uses the word 'إنكار' (denial) to emphasize rejection.
2
Identify the three denials
Note that this group denies three specific things: punishment, questioning, and the return of souls. They are interconnected.
3
Understand the consequence
They say the dead remain dead until the Day of Resurrection, implying no intermediate state.
This contrasts with the Sunni belief in an active barzakh.
4
Reflect on the source
Sanusi reports this view via transmission (نُقِلَ), indicating it is not his own view but a reported deviant opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد نُقِلَ عن ضرار وبشرِ المَرِّيسي وجماعةٍ مِنَ المعتزلة .. إنكارُ عذاب القبر والمساءلة فيه ورد الأرواح فيه إلى الأجسادِ ، وقالوا : مَنْ ماتَ فهو ميت في قبره إلى يوم القيامة. وزعم أبو الهذيلِ مِنَ المعتزلة : أنَّ مَنْ خرجَ مِنَ الدنيا على غيرِ سمةِ الإيمانِ فإِنَّهُ يُعذِّبُ بينَ النفختين ويُسأَلُ إِذْ ذاك (۱) وأثبت البلخي والجبائي وابنه عذاب القبر للكفَّارِ والفاسقين دونَ المؤمنين ، وأنكروا تسمية الملكين بمُنْكَرٍ ونَكِيرِ ، والشرع ورد بتسميتهما بذلك (٢) وقال صالح قِبَّةٌ مِنَ المعتزلة : عذاب القبر جائز ، ويجري على المؤمنينَ مِنْ غيرِ ردّ الأرواحِ إلى أجسادِها ، وقال : إنَّ الميت يجوزُ أنْ يُحِسَّ ويألم ! وهو خلافُ الضرورة . وقالَتْ طائفةٌ مِنَ الكرَّاميَّةِ والمعتزلةِ : إِنَّ اللهَ تعالى يُعذِّبُ الموتى في قبورهم ويُحدِثُ فيهمُ الألم وهم لا يشعرونَ ، فإذا أُحْيُوا وجدوا تلك الآلام ، قالوا : كالسكران إذا ضُرِبَ فَإِنَّهُ يُحِسُّ أَلمَهُ بعدُ إِذا رجعَ إليه عقله !
And it has been transmitted from Ḍirār and Bishr al-Marīsī and a group of the Mu'tazila ... the denial of the punishment of the grave and the questioning in it and the return of souls to bodies in it, and they said: Whoever dies, he is dead in his grave until the Day of Resurrection. And Abu al-Hudhayl of the Mu'tazila claimed that whoever leaves the world without the mark of faith, then he will be punished between the two trumpet blasts and will be questioned then. And al-Balkhī and al-Jubbā'ī and his son affirmed the punishment of the grave for disbelievers and sinners but not for believers, and they denied the naming of the two angels as Munkar and Nakīr, while the Sacred Law has come with their naming as such. And Ṣāliḥ Qubbah of the Mu'tazila said: The punishment of the grave is possible and it occurs to believers without returning souls to their bodies, and he said: It is possible for the dead to feel and experience pain! And that is contrary to necessity. And a group of the Karramiyya and Mu'tazila said: God Most High punishes the dead in their graves and creates in them pain while they are not aware, so when they are resurrected they find those pains. They said: Like a drunk person who is struck, then he feels his pain later when his intellect returns to him!
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage enumerates the various deviant opinions regarding the punishment of the grave. It begins with the view of Ḍirār, Bishr al-Marīsī, and a group of Mu'tazila who completely deny the punishment, questioning, and return of souls. Then it mentions Abu al-Hudhayl's view that only non-believers are punished between the two trumpet blasts. Then al-Balkhī and al-Jubbā'ī limit the punishment to disbelievers and sinners and deny the names of the angels Munkar and Nakīr. Then Ṣāliḥ Qubbah claims it is possible without returning souls, and the dead can feel pain — which the author notes is contrary to necessity. Finally, the Karramiyya and some Mu'tazila say the punishment occurs but the dead are unaware, like a drunk person.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
المساءلة
رد الأرواح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which group completely denied the punishment of the grave, the questioning, and the return of souls?
A) Ḍirār and Bishr al-Marīsī
B) Abu al-Hudhayl
C) al-Balkhī and al-Jubbā'ī
D) Ṣāliḥ Qubbah

Key Takeaway
The first deviant view recorded by Sanusi is the complete denial of the punishment of the grave by Ḍirār, Bishr al-Marīsī, and their followers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you expect to immediately meet the questioning angels and taste the reality of the grave? Or have you been living as if death is merely a long sleep? What will you change starting today to prepare for that moment?
?

?
‘Whoever dies, he is dead in his grave until the Day of Resurrection.’ Is that how you live—as if the grave is a state of nothingness? Or do you live with the urgent awareness that your soul will be returned to your body for accountability before the final day? What is one action you will take today to align your life with the truth of the grave?

Abu al-Hudhayl's View on Punishment Between the Trumpet Blasts
Sanusi presents Abu al-Hudhayl's view on grave punishment for non-believers between the trumpet blasts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu al-Hudhayl's unique claim that punishment of the grave occurs only between the two trumpet blasts and only for those who die without faith.

Core Idea
Abu al-Hudhayl limited grave punishment to a specific interim period.

After presenting the total denial, Sanusi moves to a more nuanced view from Abu al-Hudhayl of the Mu'tazila. He maintained that only those who die without the mark of faith will be punished, and that this punishment occurs specifically between the two trumpet blasts on the Day of Resurrection. This lesson explores his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and English translation to understand Abu al-Hudhayl's position.
Notice the phrase 'بين النفختين' (between the two trumpet blasts).
2
Identify who is punished
Abu al-Hudhayl says only those who leave the world 'without the mark of faith' will be punished and questioned.
3
Understand the timing
The punishment occurs 'between the two trumpet blasts' — a specific eschatological period, not immediately after death.
This differs from the Sunni view that punishment begins in the grave immediately.
4
Compare with Sunni doctrine
Consider how this view restricts the scope and timing of punishment, contrasting with the mainstream belief in universal questioning and punishment for disbelievers.
