The Reality of Barzakh and the Objection from Observation
Defends belief in barzakh using the analogy of sleep and refutes the objection from sensory observation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how belief in the unseen realities of barzakh is defended against the objection that we observe no change in the dead.

Core Idea
The unseen realities of barzakh are not disproved by observation, just as a sleeper's internal states are unseen.

This passage addresses a common objection: if we see the dead lying unchanged in their graves, how can there be punishment or bliss in the barzakh? The author, Sanusi, uses the analogy of sleep to show that internal experiences can be real without external signs. He then grounds the belief in the possibility of supernatural events reported by revelation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Recognize that some people deny barzakh events because they see no change in the dead. This is the common sense objection that the passage refutes.
The objection is based on empirical observation.
2
Examine the sleep analogy
Read how the author compares the deceased to a sleeping person: we do not observe the sleeper's internal joys and pains, yet they are real. Similarly, the dead may experience unseen states.
This shows that lack of observation does not negate reality.
3
Understand the nature of barzakh
The passage defines barzakh as the first stage of the Hereafter, where supernatural events occur. These events are not bound by normal physical laws.
Barzakh is a realm of khawariq al-'adat (supernatural occurrences).
4
Accept the authority of revelation
The author concludes that since these supernatural events are reported by shariah and are possible, we must believe in them literally, regardless of what we observe.
Faith in the unseen is central.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يشكُ في التصديقِ بذلكَ ، كيف والنائم يدرك أحوالاً مِنَ السرورِ والغمومِ والآلامِ مِنْ نفسِهِ ، ونحن لا نشاهد ذلك منه ؟! والبرزخ أوَّلُ منزلٍ مِنْ منازل الآخرة ، وفيه تغيـيـر الـعـادات وخرقُها ، فيصحُ أنْ يكونَ الميتُ حال مشاهدتنا له ، والقبر حال نظرِنا إليه .. على غيرِ الحالةِ التي نشاهدها ولم نشعر بشيء مما هنالك والأمر بيدِ اللهِ تعالى ، يُظهرُ ما يشاء ، ويَحجُبُ ما يشاءُ نسأله سبحانَهُ أنْ يجعلنا ممَّنْ آمَنَ بهِ وبملائكته وكتبه ورسله ، ويَختِمَ لنا بخواتم السعداء ، ويُؤمِّنَ روعتنا في الدنيا والآخرة. ولا يقدح فيه مشاهدتُنا للميت على نحو ما وُضِعَ في قبره ؛ لأنَّ في الموتِ وما بعدَهُ خوارق عادات أخبر بها الشرعُ ، وهي جائزةٌ ، فوجب الإيمان بها على ظاهرها.
One does not doubt in believing that, for how [can one deny] while the sleeping person experiences states of joy, grief, and pain from within himself, and we do not observe that from him? And the barzakh is the first stage of the stages of the Hereafter, and in it there is alteration of customs and breaking of them, so it is valid that the deceased, at the time of our observing him, and the grave, at the time of our looking at it, are in a state other than the state that we observe, and we have not perceived anything of what is there. And the matter is in the hand of Allah Most High; He manifests what He wills and conceals what He wills. We ask Him, glorified is He, to make us among those who believe in Him, His angels, His books, and His messengers, and to seal for us with the seals of the happy ones, and to secure our terror in this world and the Hereafter. And our observation of the deceased in the manner he was placed in his grave does not detract from it; because in death and what follows it there are supernatural events that the Law has reported, and they are possible, so it is necessary to believe in them according to their apparent meaning.
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the objection that observing the dead in their graves contradicts the reality of barzakh and its events. The author first uses the analogy of sleep: a sleeping person experiences internal states of joy, grief, and pain that we do not observe externally. Similarly, the deceased may be in a different unseen state. Then he affirms that barzakh is the first stage of the Hereafter where supernatural events occur, so the state of the dead and the grave can be different from what we perceive. He then explicitly states that our observation of the dead does not invalidate the belief in the unseen realities of death, because shariah has informed us of supernatural events (khawariq al-'adat) that occur in death and thereafter, and since these are possible (ja'iz), we must accept them literally. The passage ends with a supplication.

Key Terms
البرزخ
خوارق العادات
عذاب القبر
الإيمان بالغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because we see no change in the dead, there is no life in the barzakh.
Correction: The author argues that just as a sleeper experiences unseen joys and pains, the deceased may be in a different state. Moreover, death involves supernatural events (khawariq al-'adat) that are beyond normal observation, so our sight does not disprove them.

B) A sleeping person's internal experiences
C) A dream vision

Key Takeaway
Belief in barzakh and its events is obligatory because they are possible and reported by revelation, even if not observable.

?

Necessary Beliefs and the Bāṭiniyya View on the Threat
Sanusi lists necessary beliefs and partially refutes the Bāṭiniyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand some of the necessary beliefs from the unseen, the Bāṭiniyya's denial of the execution of the threat, and the partial refutation of their arguments.

Core Idea
Not all threats are scares; some are real and will be executed.

Sanusi begins a new section on specific beliefs from the unseen. He lists several matters that every Muslim must believe, then focuses on the execution of the divine threat (nufūdh al-waʿīd). He explains that three schools exist, and presents the view of the Bāṭiniyya who claim the threats are only for intimidation. Two of their proofs are given; the first is refuted, while the second remains unresolved in this passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of necessary beliefs
First, read the opening lines that enumerate beliefs like nufūdh al-waʿīd, intercession, the Basin, the Bridge, and the scrolls. Notice that these are known by necessity.
The list is not exhaustive; it includes 'other such things'.
2
Identify the three schools on nufūdh al-waʿīd
Sanusi says people have three schools on whether threats are executed. Only the first school (Bāṭiniyya) is described here. Look for the phrase 'ثلاثة مذاهب'.
3
Examine the Bāṭiniyya's first proof and its refutation
The Bāṭiniyya claim threats are only for intimidation, citing Q. 39:16. Sanusi refutes by noting the verse refers to worldly intimidation; the threat occurs in the afterlife.
This is a clear rejoinder based on context.
4
Consider the second proof and note the missing answer
Their second proof is from God's mercy: how could He torment a weak creature? The passage breaks off without a full refutation; the answer likely continues on the next page.
This lesson is based only on the present text.
5
Reflect on the significance of nufūdh al-waʿīd
Ask yourself why this belief matters. It affirms that God's warnings are real and that punishment is a just consequence for sin, while also allowing for intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان جملة ما يجب الإيمان به من الغيوب ما علم من الدين بالضرورة أو شبهها . ومما جاء به صلى الله عليه وسلم ويجب الإيمان به : نفوذ الوعيد في طائفة من عصاة أمته، ثم يخرجون بشفاعته صلى الله عليه وسلم، والحوض، وهل هو قبل الصراط أو بعده، أو هما حوضان: أحدهما قبل الصراط، والآخر، وهو الصحيح؟ أقوال، وتطاير الصحف، إلى غير ذلك مما علم من الدين ضرورة، وعلمه مفصل في الكتاب والسنة وكتب علماء الأمة بعده. اعلم : أن نفوذ الوعيد اختلف الناس فيه على ثلاثة مذاهب : الأول : أن الوعيد الوارد في الكتب الإلهية إنما جاء للتخويف فقط، وأما فعل الإيلام فلا ! وهذا قول الباطنية، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى : {ذَلِكَ يُخَوِّفُ اللَّهُ بِهِ عِبَادَهُ} [الزمر: ١٦]، ولا يخفى فساده ؛ فإن التخويف المذكور في الآية إنما هو في الدنيا، وفي الآخرة يقع المخوف به. واحتجوا أيضاً : بأن الحكيم أرحم الراحمين؛ كيف يعذب حيواناً ضعيفاً غايته أنه بمعصيته إنما قصر في حق نفسه؛ لاستحالة أن يكون الله تعالى نفع في عمل أحد أو ضرر به ؟!
A chapter on explaining the totality of what must be believed from the unseen - what is known from religion by necessity or its like. And from what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought and belief in which is obligatory: the execution of the threat against a group of the sinners of his community, then they come out through his intercession (peace be upon him); and the Basin (al-ḥawḍ); and whether it is before the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ) or after it, or there are two basins: one before the Bridge and the other, which is the correct view? - there are opinions; and the flying of the scrolls; and other such things that are known from religion by necessity, and their detailed knowledge is in the Book, the Sunnah, and the books of the scholars of the community after him. Know that the execution of the threat is something about which people have differed into three schools: First: that the threat mentioned in the divine books came only for intimidation, and as for the actual infliction of pain, no! This is the saying of the Bāṭiniyya. They adduced His saying, the Most High: '{That is how Allah threatens His servants}' [al-Zumar: 16] - and its corruption is not hidden; for the intimidation mentioned in the verse is only in this world, and in the Hereafter the threatened thing occurs. And they also adduced: that the Wise is the Most Merciful of the merciful; how could He torment a weak animal whose ultimate limit is that by his disobedience he only fell short in his own right, given the impossibility that Allah, the Most High, benefits from anyone's action or is harmed by it?!
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage begins a new section (faṣl) on the beliefs that are obligatory from the unseen. It first enumerates several specific beliefs: the execution of the divine threat (nufūdh al-waʿīd) for a group of sinful Muslims who will later be brought out by the Prophet's intercession; the Basin (al-ḥawḍ); the debate about its timing relative to the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ); the flying of the scrolls (taṭāyur al-ṣuḥuf); and other matters known by necessity from religion. Then it focuses on the differing views regarding nufūdh al-waʿīd, stating that there are three schools. Only the first school is detailed here: the Bāṭiniyya claim that the threats in scripture are merely for intimidation and not actually carried out. Two of their proofs are presented. The author immediately refutes the first proof by noting that the verse they cite refers to intimidation in this world, whereas the threatened punishment occurs in the afterlife. The second proof, based on God's mercy, is left without a direct refutation in this window; the text breaks off, likely to be continued on the next page. Thus, the lesson covers the exposition of the Bāṭiniyya position and a partial refutation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Bāṭiniyya believe that God's threats in scripture are only meant to scare people, not to be actually carried out, because God is too merciful to punish.
Correction: The author refutes the first proof by showing that the verse they cite refers to intimidation in this world, while the punishment occurs in the Hereafter. The second proof is left unrefuted in this passage.

Checkpoint
What is the first proof of the Bāṭiniyya that the author refutes in this passage?
A) God is too merciful to punish.
B) The Quranic verse about threatening is only for this world.
C) Punishment is impossible because God does not benefit from actions.
D) Sinners are not really responsible.

Key Takeaway
The Bāṭiniyya denied the execution of the threat, arguing from a verse about intimidation and from God's mercy, but the first argument is refuted by distinguishing worldly intimidation from afterlife punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Essential Eschatological Beliefs: Known by Necessity
Sanusi enumerates essential unseen beliefs from revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that certain eschatological beliefs, such as the Pool and intercession, are considered known by necessity in Islam and are obligatory to believe.

Core Idea
Some unseen beliefs are so clear that they are known by religious necessity.

This passage introduces a set of key eschatological beliefs that every Muslim must affirm. Sanusi emphasizes that these matters are not speculative; they are established by revelation and known by necessity. As you read, notice how he categorizes these beliefs and the level of certainty they carry.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Carefully read the Arabic and English translation. Note the list of beliefs mentioned.
The passage is a chapter heading, so it sets the stage.
2
Identify the key beliefs
List the specific eschatological events Sanusi mentions: execution of threat, intercession, the Pool, the Bridge, and scattering of scrolls.
These are all from the samiyyat (revelational matters).
3
Understand 'known by necessity'
Reflect on what it means for something to be known by necessity (ضرورة) in the religion. It means these are so clear that no Muslim can deny them without leaving the fold.
Sanusi says these are detailed in the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان جمله ما يجب الایمان به من الغيوب ما علم من الدين بالضرورة أو شبهها ومما جاء به صلى الله عليه وسلم ويجب الإيمان به : نفوذ الوعيد في طائفة من عصاة أمته ، ثم يخرجون بشفاعته صلى الله عليه وسلم ، والحوض ، وهل هو قبل الصراط أو بعده ، أو هما حوضان : أحدهما قبل الصراط ، والآخر ، وهو الصحيح ؟ أقوال ، وتطاير الصحف ، إلى غير ذلك مما علم من الدين ضرورة ، وعلمه مفصل في الكتاب والسنة وكتب علماء الأمة بعده.
Chapter: On explaining the sum of what must be believed from the unseen, those things known from the religion by necessity or its likeness. And among what he (peace be upon him) brought and must be believed is: the execution of the threat for a group of the disobedient of his nation, then they will come out by his intercession (peace be upon him), and the Pool, and whether it is before the Bridge or after, or they are two Pools: one before the Bridge and the other – and that is the correct opinion? – different sayings, and the scattering of the scrolls, and other things known from the religion by necessity, and its knowledge is detailed in the Book, the Sunnah, and the books of the scholars of the nation after him.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage is a chapter introduction that lists several key eschatological beliefs which are considered known by necessity (ضرورة) in Islam. Sanusi emphasizes that these matters are from the unseen (غيوب) and that they must be believed because they are clearly established in the religion. He specifically mentions the execution of the threat (نفوذ الوعيد) – that some sinful Muslims will be punished but later rescued through the Prophet's intercession. He also mentions the Pool (الحوض) and notes a scholarly difference on whether it is before or after the Bridge (صراط), or if there are two Pools. The scattering of scrolls (تطاير الصحف) is another example. Sanusi concludes that these matters are detailed in the Quran, Sunnah, and the works of the scholars, indicating that they are not speculative but firmly grounded in revelation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think these eschatological details are minor or optional to believe.
Correction: Sanusi asserts they are known by necessity from the religion, meaning denying them is tantamount to denying clear revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how are the listed eschatological beliefs known?
A) Through rational deduction
B) Through analogy
C) By necessity from the religion
D) Through personal experience

Key Takeaway
Eschatological beliefs like the Pool and intercession are obligatory to affirm because they are known by necessity from revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that the execution of the threat will happen to some sinful believers. Think of a sin you committed recently. Do you truly fear that it might subject you to that punishment, or do you comfort yourself with a vague hope of automatic forgiveness? What would it mean for you today to live with the certainty that the threat is real?
?
The passage insists these eschatological events are known by necessity—not optional. Does your daily life reflect the same urgency about the Pool, the Bridge, and the scattering of scrolls as it does about your next meal? If not, which of these realities do you need to confront most honestly, and what step will you take tonight to let it change how you live?
?
You have learned that intercession depends on the Prophet's permission. Imagine standing on the Day of Judgment with your scroll in hand. Will you be among those for whom the Prophet intercedes? What are you doing right now to secure that intercession, and what are you doing that might forfeit it?

The Third Opinion on Punishment and the Division of People
Sanusi presents the third opinion on punishment and the division of people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on the punishment of sinners, how it differs from the Mu'tazila, and how people are divided into categories with different fates.

Core Idea
Divine mercy and will, not reason alone, determine sinners' punishment.

This passage presents the third of three opinions on punishment, affirming that punishment is good for both disbelievers and sinful believers. However, Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila differ on why it is good and whether it is eternal. Sanusi then lays out the full categorization of people—believers and disbelievers—explaining the fate of each group according to Ahl al-Sunna consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third opinion
Notice that punishment is good for all sinners, but Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila share this view for different reasons. Read the opening two sentences carefully.
2
Understand the Ahl al-Sunna qualifications
Note that punishment is not eternal for sinful believers and not all sinners are punished, because God may pardon. This is a key difference from Mu'tazila.
See phrases 'ليس دائما' and 'لا شاملا'.
3
Map the division of people
Follow the classification that starts with 'الناس على قسمين'. Identify the two main categories and their subcategories until the end.
Pay attention to the branching: believer vs disbeliever, then protected vs not protected, etc.
4
Summarize the fates
For each category, determine the final outcome as stated: disbelievers eternally in Fire, protected believers immediately in Paradise, others under God's will with possible punishment or pardon.
The last part mentions consensus that threat is carried out on some but not all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الثالث : أن العذاب ثابت حسن في حق الكفار وعصاة المؤمنين ، وهذا هو الذي أجمع عليه أهل السنة والمعتزلة ، إلا أن حسنه عند أهل السنة بالشرع ، وعند المعتزلة بالعقل ، وأيضا : فليس دائما هو في حق من نفذ فيه من عصاة المؤمنين عند أهل السنة ولا شاملا عندهم لجميع العصاة ؛ لثبوت عفوه تعالى عن كثير . وخالف المعتزلة في الأمرين وبالجملة : فمذهب جميع أهل الحق وأهل السنة : أن الناس على قسمين : مؤمن وكافر ؛ فالكافر في النار مخلد فيها بإجماع ، والمؤمن على ضربين : محفوظ من المعاصي عمره وغير محفوظ ؛ فالأول : في الجنة بدءا بالإجماع ، والثاني : صاحب صغائر وصاحب كبائر ، وصاحب الكبائر : تائب وغير تائب ، فالقسمان الأولان أيضا في الجنة أبدا بإجماع ، وربما تكون بعد أهوال ثم يغفر الله سبحانه ، وغير التائب في مشيئة الله تعالى ، مع إجماعهم على نفوذ الوعيد في بعضهم ؛ وهو جماعة من كل نوع من أنواع المعاصي
The third opinion: that punishment is established and good for disbelievers and sinful believers, and this is what the Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila agreed upon, except that its goodness with Ahl al-Sunna is by the Law (shar'), and with the Mu'tazila by reason ('aql). Also: it is not perpetual for those of the sinful believers who are subject to it according to Ahl al-Sunna, nor is it all-encompassing for all sinners, due to the establishment of His pardon for many. And the Mu'tazila opposed in both matters. In summary: the doctrine of all the people of truth and Ahl al-Sunna is that people are of two divisions: believer and disbeliever; the disbeliever is in the Fire, eternally [abiding] therein by consensus. The believer is of two types: one who is protected from sin throughout his life and one who is not protected. The first is in Paradise from the start by consensus. The second is a committer of minor sins and a committer of major sins. The committer of major sins is repentant and non-repentant. So the first two categories are also in Paradise forever by consensus, possibly after terrors, then God forgives. The non-repentant is under the will of God, with their consensus that the threat is carried out on some of them, namely a group from every type of sins.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage presents the third opinion on punishment and details the Ahl al-Sunna view on the final fate of people. It begins by stating the common ground between Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila: punishment is good and established for both disbelievers and sinful believers. However, the basis of its goodness differs: for Ahl al-Sunna it is by the Law (shar'), for Mu'tazila by reason ('aql). Then it clarifies that according to Ahl al-Sunna, punishment for sinful believers is not eternal nor all-encompassing, because God may pardon many. The author then summarizes the complete doctrine: people are divided into believers and disbelievers. Disbelievers are eternally in Hell. Believers are of two types: those preserved from sin (the prophets), and those not preserved. The preserved believer enters Paradise immediately. The latter type includes those who commit only minor sins and those who commit major sins. The major sinner may repent or not. Those with minor sins and repentant major sinners enter Paradise after any purgation. The unrepentant major sinner is subject to God's will; some will be punished, as there is consensus that the divine threat is carried out on some sinners. This section establishes the nuanced Ahl al-Sunna position against the Mu'tazila who believe in eternal punishment for all unrepentant sinners.

Key Terms
عذاب
حسن
شرع
عقل
مخلد
مشيئة
عفو
نفوذ الوعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ahl al-Sunna believe all sinful believers are punished eternally.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna distinguish categories: minor sinners and repentant major sinners eventually enter Paradise, and unrepentant major sinners may be forgiven by God's will; punishment is not necessarily eternal or universal for sinful believers.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna, what is the basis for the goodness of punishment for sinners?
A) Reason (al-'aql)
B) The Law (al-shar')
C) Both reason and the Law
D) Consensus of the community

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Sunna view on punishment balances divine justice and mercy: God's will and pardon override strict rational accountability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own sins, do you truly place yourself under God's will, fearing His justice while hoping for His pardon? How does this lesson challenge you to neither despair nor become complacent in your repentance?
?
This lesson distinguishes between reason and divine law. In what areas of your life are you tempted to rely on your own sense of right and wrong rather than submitting to God's command? What would it look like to surrender that area to Him today?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you be among the protected or the non-protected? Based on this lesson, what is your standing before God? What concrete step can you take today to ensure you are among those who receive His mercy?

The Prophet's Intercession for Sinful Believers
Sanusi affirms the Prophet's intercession and states the Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine of the Prophet's intercession for sinful believers and the Mu'tazila rejection based on their principle of eternal punishment.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession removes sinful believers from Hellfire—a mercy denied by the Mu'tazila.

This passage addresses a key point of contention between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila: whether the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) can intercede for believers who die in a state of major sin. The Sunni position is clear and emphatic, while the Mu'tazila's rationalist theology leads them to deny it. We will explore both sides and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the confident tone of the author when stating the Sunni position.
The phrase 'لا خفاء في ثبوتها' indicates consensus.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents the Sunni affirmation and the Mu'tazila denial. Mark each and note the reason given for the denial.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila principle
The Mu'tazila deny intercession because they believe the wicked (fasiq) is eternally in the Fire like the disbeliever. This means there is no removal from Hell for such a person.
This principle stems from their view that grave sin removes one from faith but does not make one a disbeliever, yet punishment is eternal.
4
Note other intercessions and the prayer
The author mentions that the Prophet has other intercessions recorded in hadith and ends with a prayer not to be deprived of them.
This shows the breadth of prophetic intercession beyond just removal from Hell.
5
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider why this issue matters: it relates to God's mercy, justice, and the Prophet's status. How does intercession balance divine justice with mercy?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما شفاعة سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في إخراج عصاة المؤمنين من النار : فلا خفاء في ثبوتها عند أهل السنة ، وأنكرها المعتزلة على أصلهم في أن الفاسق مخلد في النار كالكافر ، ولنبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم شفاعات أخر مشهورة في كتب الحديث ، نسأله سبحانه أن لا يحرمنا منها
As for the intercession of our master and leader Muhammad (may God bless him and grant him peace) for the removal of sinful believers from the Fire: there is no obscurity in its establishment according to Ahl al-Sunna, and the Mu'tazila denied it based on their principle that the wicked (fāsiq) is eternally in the Fire like the disbeliever. And our Prophet and leader Muhammad (may God bless him and grant him peace) has other well-known intercessions in the books of hadith. We ask Him, glorified, not to deprive us of them.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage focuses on the doctrine of the Prophet's intercession (shafā'a). It states that intercession for the removal of sinful believers from Hellfire is well-established (lā khafā') among Ahl al-Sunna. The Mu'tazila denied it because their principle holds that the wicked (fāsiq), like the disbeliever, is eternally in the Fire. The text then notes that the Prophet has other intercessions recorded in hadith collections, and the author prays not to be deprived of them.

Key Terms
شفاعة
إخراج
عصاة
مخلد
فاسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is only for disbelievers or that it applies to everyone without distinction.
Correction: The passage specifies that the intercession in question is for sinful believers (عصاة المؤمنين) to remove them from Hell, not for disbelievers. The Mu'tazila denial is based on their view that such believers are eternally punished, so intercession would be ineffective.

Checkpoint
Why did the Mu'tazila deny the Prophet's intercession for sinful believers?
A) They believed the Prophet never intercedes.
B) They held that the wicked (fāsiq) is eternally in the Fire like a disbeliever.
C) They thought intercession is only for the living.
D) They rejected the concept of sin altogether.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession for sinful believers is a confirmed Sunni doctrine, denied by the Mu'tazila because they hold that the fasiq suffers eternal punishment like a disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly rely on the Prophet's intercession while also striving to repent and avoid sin, or do you treat it as a license to keep sinning? What will you change today to show you are serious about both hope and action?
?
The Mu'tazila let their own reasoning block them from accepting a mercy that Allah has promised through His Prophet. Is there any belief or assumption you hold that might be preventing you from fully embracing a clear teaching of the Quran and Sunna? Will you submit to revelation even when it challenges your logic?
?
If the Prophet's intercession can remove a sinful believer from Hell, how does that reshape your view of a fellow Muslim who struggles with sins? Will you now see them as a potential recipient of mercy rather than writing them off, and will you pray for the Prophet's intercession to include them?

The Prophet's Pool: Established Reality and Twofold Nature
Sanusi affirms the Pool and explains the disagreement on its timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's Pool (ḥawḍ) is a well-established reality in Sunni belief, and that scholars differ on its timing, with the verified view being that there are two pools—one before and one after the Bridge (ṣirāṭ).

Core Idea
The Prophet has two pools: one before the Bridge, one after.

Sanusi affirms the reality of the Prophet's Pool as a well-known and widespread matter of faith. He then addresses a scholarly disagreement about whether the Pool occurs before or after the Ṣirāṭ Bridge, resolving it with the position that the Prophet actually possesses two pools. This lesson clarifies this important eschatological detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Let Sanusi's own words set the context.
2
Identify the three key elements
Notice the sequence: (1) affirmation that the Pool is well-known, (2) a personal prayer, (3) the disagreement on timing, and (4) the resolution of two pools.
The author resolves disagreement by stating there are two pools.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why having two pools matters. One comes before the Bridge, offering solace; the other after, rewarding the righteous. The prayer shows the author's hope to be among the first.
This connects to the broader theme of intercession and divine mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ثبوت الحوض له صلى الله عليه وسلم : فمشهور مستفيض ، نسأله سبحانه أن يجعلنا في الرعيل الأول من الواردين منه . واختلفوا : هل هو قبل الصراط أو بعده ؟ والتحقيق : أن له حوضين : قبل ، وبعد .
As for the establishment of the Pool (al-ḥawḍ) for him (may God bless him and grant him peace): it is well-known and widespread. We ask Him, glorified, to make us among the first band of those who drink from it. And they differed: is it before the Bridge (ṣirāṭ) or after? The verification: that he has two pools: before and after.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage addresses the reality of the Prophet's Pool (ḥawḍ). It states that its existence is well-known and widely transmitted (mashhūr mustafīḍ). The author prays to be among the first to drink from it. Then it notes a disagreement: is the Pool before or after the Bridge (ṣirāṭ)? The verified position (taḥqīq) is that the Prophet actually has two pools: one before the Bridge and one after.

Key Terms
حوض
صراط
رعيل
مستفيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is only one pool for the Prophet.
Correction: The verified view is that the Prophet has two pools: one before the Bridge and one after, as stated by Sanusi.

Checkpoint
What is the verified opinion regarding the number of pools for the Prophet?
A) There is only one pool after the Bridge.
B) There is only one pool before the Bridge.
C) There are two pools, one before and one after the Bridge.
D) The pool is not real but metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet has two pools: one before the Ṣirāṭ and one after, harmonizing the scholarly disagreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Do you truly long for that moment in your daily life, or do worldly desires distract you from that hope? What one change can you make today to align your heart with that aspiration?
?
The passage resolves a disagreement by stating that there are two pools, one before the Ṣirāṭ and one after. This requires accepting a truth that may differ from your initial expectation. In your own life, when faced with a contradiction in Islamic teachings, do you seek a resolution that honors all evidence, or do you rush to side with one opinion? What specific issue have you been avoiding reconciling?
?
The author prays to be among the 'first band' to drink from the Pool. If you were to stand before the Pool today, would you be among the first, or would hesitation and sins hold you back? What is one sin you need to sincerely repent from to have hope of being among the first?

The Flying Scrolls and the Book of the Sinful Believer
Sanusi mentions the flying scrolls and discusses whether the sinful believer receives his book in the right hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate about whether the sinful believer who is punished receives his book in the right hand, and why the author favors suspending judgment.

Core Idea
For the punished believer, receiving the book in the right hand is not certain—it is best left suspended.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses an eschatological detail: the flying of the scrolls. While the event itself is well-known, a question arises about the sinful believer who actually faces punishment. Does he still receive his book in his right hand, or is his case uncertain? Sanusi points to the safer view: suspension of judgment.

Guided Path
1
Understand the event
Recognize that the flying scrolls (taṭāyur al-ṣuḥuf) is a well-known eschatological event. This sets the context.
The event is established in the sources.
2
Identify the issue
Notice the disagreement: for the sinful believer who actually undergoes punishment, does he receive his book in his right hand?
This is a specific question about honor even after punishment.
3
See the preferred view
The author states that suspending judgment (muwaqqaf) is closer to the truth. This means we do not affirm either hand, leaving it to Allah.
This shows scholarly caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تطاير الصحف : فمشهور أيضاً واختلفوا فيمن ينفذ فيه الوعيد من عصاة المؤمنين : هل يأخذ كتابه بيمينه ، أو أمره موقوف؟ وهو أقرب ، والله تعالى أعلم .
As for the flying of the scrolls (taṭāyur al-ṣuḥuf): it is also well-known. And they differed concerning those of the sinful believers upon whom the threat is executed: does he take his book in his right hand, or is his matter suspended? And that (i.e., suspension) is closer, and God Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage deals with the eschatological event of the flying of scrolls (taṭāyur al-ṣuḥuf), stating it is well-known. It then raises a question: regarding the sinful believer who is actually punished (upon whom the threat is executed), will he receive his book (record of deeds) in his right hand (a sign of honor), or is his matter suspended (muwaqqaf)? The author states that suspension is the closer (aqrab) opinion, but leaves final knowledge to God.

Key Terms
تطاير الصحف
كتاب بيمينه
موقوف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that all believers, regardless of punishment, will receive their book in the right hand.
Correction: This passage indicates that for believers who are actually punished, it is not certain that they receive their book in the right hand; the safer view is to suspend judgment.

Checkpoint
What is the author's preferred view regarding the sinful believer who is punished: does he receive his book in the right hand?
A) He definitely receives it in the right hand.
B) He does not receive it at all.
C) His matter is suspended, and that is closer to the truth.
D) He receives it in the left hand.

Key Takeaway
For the sinful believer who is punished, it is more cautious to suspend judgment regarding whether they receive their book in the right hand.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own sins, do you assume you will still receive your book in your right hand because you are a believer, or does the possibility of your matter being suspended (موقوف) trouble you? How would this uncertainty change the way you approach repentance today?
?
Sanusi leaves the final knowledge to Allah. Are you comfortable with not knowing your ultimate fate, or do you try to guarantee your salvation through your own deeds? What would it look like to live with both hope and fear, trusting Allah's wisdom over your own assumptions?

The Prophet's Basin: Affirmation and Timing
The author affirms the Prophet's basin and resolves the timing debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Prophet's Hawd, its wide transmission, and the verified view regarding its timing relative to the Sirat.

Core Idea
The Prophet has two basins: one before the Sirat and one after.

The belief in the Prophet's Basin (al-Hawd) is an established component of Sunni eschatology. The author begins by affirming its authenticity as widely transmitted, then turns to a scholarly debate: is the Hawd before or after the Sirat? The passage presents the verified resolution, which harmonizes both opinions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the key term 'مستفيض' which indicates the wide transmission of this belief.
2
Identify the two issues
The passage covers two things: first, the affirmation of the Hawd; second, the timing. Identify the author's prayer and the difference of opinion.
3
Understand the resolution
The verified position states there are two basins. Reflect on how this resolves the debate and what it implies for the believer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ثبوت الحوض له صلى الله عليه وسلم: فمشهور مستفيض، نسأله سبحانه أن يجعلنا في الرعيل الأول من الواردين منه. واختلفوا: هل هو قبل الصراط أو بعده؟ والتحقيق: أن له حوضين: قبل، وبعد.
And as for the establishment of the Basin (al-Hawd) for him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: it is well-known and widely transmitted. We ask Him Glorified to make us among the first group of those who drink from it. And they differed: is it before the Sirat or after it? And the verified position is that he has two basins: one before and one after.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of the Prophet's Hawd (basin) as a well-known and widely transmitted doctrine. The author then prays to be among the first to drink from it. There is a difference of opinion regarding whether the Hawd is before or after the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). The author states that the verified position (al-tahqiq) is that the Prophet has two basins: one before the Sirat and one after. This resolves the debate by allowing both.

Key Terms
الحوض
الصراط
مستفيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is only one basin, either before or after the Sirat.
Correction: The verified position is that the Prophet has two basins: one before the Sirat and one after.

Checkpoint
What is the author's verified position regarding the Prophet's Basin?
A) It is only before the Sirat.
B) It is only after the Sirat.
C) He has two basins: one before and one after the Sirat.
D) The basin is not established according to the verified position.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet has two basins: one before the Sirat and one after, confirming the wide transmission of this doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you actively hoping and striving to be among the first group to drink from the Prophet's basin? What specific steps are you taking today to qualify for that honor?
?
If you truly believed that the Prophet has prepared a basin for you after the Sirat, how would your fear of crossing that bridge change? Are you preparing now for that moment?
?
The Prophet's basin is a gift of mercy—do you thirst for it more than you thirst for anything in this world? What does your daily pursuit of worldly pleasures say about that claim?

Distribution of Scrolls and the Status of Sinful Believers
Sanusi presents a difference of opinion on sinful believers' scrolls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic scholarly difference regarding whether sinful believers receive their scroll of deeds in the right hand or if their status is suspended.

Core Idea
The fate of sinful believers' scrolls is an unsettled matter.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a subtle point within the eschatological event of the distribution of scrolls. While it is well-known that every person will receive their record of deeds, there is a question concerning those sinful believers who are subject to punishment. The author presents two scholarly positions and indicates which is more plausible.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the topic
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the topic is the 'flying of the scrolls' (تطاير الصحف) and a specific difference of opinion about sinful believers.
The passage is concise; focus on the two opinions.
2
Examine the two opinions
Identify the two views: (1) the sinful believer takes his book in the right hand, (2) his affair is suspended (موقوف). Understand that the suspension means we do not know whether he receives it in the right or left.
The phrase 'أمره موقوف' indicates uncertainty.
3
Reflect on the author's stance
Sanusi says the suspended view is 'closer' (أقرب) but ends with 'Allah knows best'. This shows scholarly caution. Consider why this position might be preferred.
The author does not definitively settle the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تطاير الصحف: فمشهور أيضاً واختلفوا فيمن ينفذ فيه الوعيد من عصاة المؤمنين: هل يأخذ كتابه بيمينه، أو أمره موقوف؟ وهو أقرب، والله تعالى أعلم.
And as for the flying of the scrolls (al-Suhuf): it is also well-known. And they differed concerning the one upon whom the threat (of punishment) is executed from among the sinful believers: does he take his book in his right hand, or is his affair suspended? And it is closer, and Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage addresses the eschatological event of the flying of the scrolls (where each person receives their record of deeds). The author affirms it as well-known. Then he mentions a difference of opinion regarding those sinful believers who will actually be punished: whether they will receive their book in the right hand (as a sign of honor) or whether their status is suspended (i.e., not determined whether they receive it in the right or left). The author leans toward the latter being closer (aqrab), but concludes with 'Allah knows best.'

Key Terms
تطاير الصحف
الوعيد
عصاة المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All believers, even sinful ones, will receive their scroll in the right hand.
Correction: The passage shows that for sinful believers who are punished, their affair may be suspended; it is not certain they receive it in the right hand.

Checkpoint
Regarding sinful believers on whom punishment is executed, what is the author's closer opinion about receiving their book?
A) They definitely take it in the right hand.
B) They definitely take it in the left hand.
C) Their affair is suspended (موقوف).
D) They do not receive a book at all.

Key Takeaway
The author favors suspending judgment on whether sinful believers who are punished receive their scroll in the right hand, acknowledging that Allah knows best.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that you are a sinner. If Allah punishes you for your sins, do you have any guarantee that you will receive your book in your right hand? How does this uncertainty affect your view of your own deeds today?
?
The author says the matter is 'suspended' and ends with 'Allahu a'lam'. How often do you act as if you know your final outcome? What would change if you truly lived with this suspension?
?
This passage concerns those 'upon whom the threat is executed.' If you fear you might be among them, what concrete steps will you take today to seek Allah's pardon before that day?

The 'Adalah of All Companions: Evidence and Doctrine
Commentator states that all Companions are 'udul and provides Quranic and Hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that all Companions are upright ('udul) and the scriptural evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
The uprightness of all Companions is a fundamental principle established by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

This passage presents the definitive position of Sunni scholarship: every proven Companion is considered upright without need for investigation. The commentator cites explicit Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths to demonstrate that the moral integrity of the Companions is a matter of divine confirmation, not human scrutiny. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English side by side to understand the flow of the argument.
Notice the strong opening statement.
2
Identify the core claim
The passage asserts that all Companions are upright and that this is the position of the majority.
This is a claim about a group of people.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
List the three Quranic verses cited and see how each supports the uprightness of the Companions.
Each verse praises the Companions collectively.
4
Examine the Hadith evidence
List the three hadiths cited and see how each supports the doctrine.
These hadiths emphasize the special status of the Companions.
5
Understand the conclusion
The commentator concludes that the correct view is that all are upright without distinction.
This is the established Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولُه : ( والصحابةُ كلُّهم عدول ) هذا هو الذي عليه جمهورُ العلماء والمحققونَ مِنْ أهلِ الأصولِ ؛ أنَّ كلَّ مَنْ ثبَتَتْ صحبتُهُ لا يُسأل عن عدالتِهِ ، ولا يُتوقَّفُ في روايتِهِ ، عُرِفَ أو لم يُعرَفْ ودليلهم : ظاهرُ الكتاب والسنَّةِ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ أَشِدَّاءُ عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَاءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ... [الفتح : ۲۹] الآيةَ ، وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْتَكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطًا ...) [البقرة : ١٤٣] الآيةَ ، وقوله : ( كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ ﴾ : أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ ... [آل عمران : ۱۱۰] الآيةَ ، وقولِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَصْحَابِي كَالنُّجُوم ؛ بِأَيْهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ أَهْتَدَيْتُمْ ) ، وقوله : « خَيْرُ الْقُرُونِ قَرْنِي » ، وقولِهِ : « لَوْ أَنْفَقَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَباً مَا بَلَغَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِمْ وَلَا نَصِيفَهُ » وفي المسألة أقوال أُخَرُ غيرُ مرضيَّة ، ومحلها علمُ الأصول والذي عليه الكتاب والسنة وإجماعُ مَنْ يُعتَدُّ بإجماعِهِ .. ما تقدَّمَ ؛ وهو أنَّهم كلهم عدولٌ مِنْ غير تفصيل .
His saying: 'And the Companions, all of them, are upright.' This is the position of the majority of scholars and investigators among the people of usul: that everyone whose companionship is established is not asked about his uprightness, nor is hesitation made regarding his narration, whether known or unknown. Their evidence is the apparent meaning of the Book and the Sunnah, such as His statement exalted: 'And those who are with him are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves...' [al-Fath 48:29] the verse, and His statement exalted: 'And thus We have made you a middle nation...' [al-Baqarah 2:143] the verse, and His statement: 'You are the best nation brought forth for mankind...' [Aal 'Imran 3:110] the verse, and his saying, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'My companions are like stars; by whichever of them you follow, you will be guided,' and his saying: 'The best of centuries is my century,' and his saying: 'If one of you were to spend the equivalent of Uhud in gold, he would not reach the mudd of one of them nor half of it.' And in this issue there are other unsatisfactory views, and their place is the science of usul. And what the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of those whose consensus is considered indicate is what preceded: that they are all upright without distinction.
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and defense of the doctrine that all Companions of the Prophet (ṣaḥāba) are inherently upright (ʿudūl) and trustworthy in matters of transmission. The commentator begins by reporting a statement attributed to the author (Sanusi) that 'the Companions, all of them, are upright.' He then affirms that this is the position of the majority of scholars and investigators in uṣūl al-fiqh. The key claim is that anyone whose companionship with the Prophet is established (thabatat ṣuḥbatuhu) is not to be examined for his moral uprightness, nor is his narration to be held in abeyance, whether his personal character is known or not. This is a strong presumption of integrity that spares one from having to investigate each Companion's 'adāla. The commentator then provides the evidence (dalīl) from the apparent meanings (ẓāhir) of the Qur'an and Sunnah. He cites four proofs: 1) Qur'anic verse 48:29 praising those with the Prophet; 2) verse 2:143 calling the Muslim community 'a middle nation'; 3) verse 3:110 calling them 'the best nation'; 4) several prophetic hadiths: 'My companions are like stars...'; 'The best of centuries is my century'; and a hadith that the expenditure of one of them (a Companion) cannot be matched by anyone after them. The commentator then mentions that there are other unsatisfactory opinions (aqwāl ukhar ghayr marḍiyya) on this issue, but notes that they belong to the science of uṣūl. He concludes that the correct view, supported by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus of reliable scholars, is what has preceded: that all Companions are upright without any distinction.

Key Terms
عدول
صحابة
عدالة
كتاب
سنة
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the uprightness of each Companion must be individually verified like other narrators.
Correction: The passage states that once companionship is established, no investigation is needed because the Quran and Sunnah collectively attest to their integrity.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the basis for not investigating the 'adalah of a Companion once his companionship is established?
A) Consensus of the Companions themselves
B) Apparent meaning of the Qur'an and Sunnah
C) Rational necessity
D) The need to accept all narrations

Key Takeaway
The doctrine that all Companions are upright is firmly established by the clear evidence of the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely accept the uprightness of all the Companions, even those whose actions you may not fully understand or that conflict with your personal judgments? What would change in your heart if you truly submitted to this principle?
?
The hadith says, 'My companions are like stars—whichever you follow, you are guided.' How does this challenge your tendency to pick and choose which Companions to follow based on personal preference or sectarian affiliation? Are you willing to follow any Companion without reservation?

Definition of a Companion and Refining the Criteria
Commentator defines Sahabi and critiques alternative wordings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of a Sahabi according to the majority and why the phrase 'man ijitama'a' is preferred over 'man ra'ahu'.

Core Idea
A Companion is defined by meeting the Prophet in faith, not by length of companionship or sight.

The commentator begins by reaffirming the consensus on the uprightness of all Companions. He then provides a technical definition of a Sahabi, explaining why the word 'meeting' is more accurate than 'seeing'. This lesson clarifies the criteria of Companionship and the honor it confers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation, to grasp the commentator's argument.
2
Identify the definition and its implications
Notice that the definition includes those who met the Prophet even briefly and even if they didn't narrate hadiths.
3
Compare the two wordings
Understand why 'man ijitama'a' is preferred over 'man ra'ahu' and how it includes blind Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المسألة أقوال أُخَرُ غيرُ مرضيَّة ، ومحلها علمُ الأصول والذي عليه الكتاب والسنة وإجماعُ مَنْ يُعتَدُّ بإجماعِهِ .. ما تقدَّمَ ؛ وهو أنَّهم كلهم عدولٌ مِنْ غير تفصيل . والصحابي عندَ الجمهورِ : مَنِ اجتمعَ مؤمناً معَ النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في حياتِهِ ، ثم مات مؤمناً وإن لم يرو عنه وإن لم يُطِلْ وقوله : (مَن اجتمعَ ( أحسنُ مِنْ قول ابن الحاجب : ( مَنْ رآه ) ؛ لأنَّه يخرجُ عنه مثلُ عبد الله بن أم مكتوم رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه ، وإنَّما لم يُشترط طولُ الاجتماع في حقّ الصاحب بالنسبة إليهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، مَعَ اشتراطِ ذلكَ فيهِ لغةً وعُرْفاً بالنسبة إلى غيرِه.. لأنَّ اجتماع المؤمنِ مَعَهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وإِنْ كانَ لحظةٌ يحصلُ لَهُ مِنَ الشرفِ ما لا يحصلُ لغيرِهِ .
And in this issue there are other unsatisfactory views, and their place is the science of usul. And what the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of those whose consensus is considered indicate is what preceded: that they are all upright without distinction. And the Sahabi according to the majority is: the one who met the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in faith during his lifetime, then died as a believer, even if he did not narrate from him and even if he did not prolong [the companionship]. And his saying (man ijitama'a) is better than Ibn al-Hajib's saying (man ra'ahu), because it excludes someone like 'Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum, may Allah be pleased with him. And indeed length of companionship is not required regarding the Companion relative to him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, even though it is required linguistically and customarily relative to others, because the believer's meeting with him, even if for a moment, obtains for him an honor that is not obtained by others.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the 'adalah of the Companions and provides a technical definition of who qualifies as a 'Sahabi' (Companion). The commentator begins by reiterating that the correct view, based on the Book, Sunnah, and consensus, is that all Companions are upright without any distinction. He then reports the definition of a Sahabi according to the majority (jumhūr): one who met the Prophet (peace be upon him) in faith during his lifetime and died as a believer, even if he did not narrate any hadith from him and even if his companionship was short. The commentator then offers a critical note: the phrase 'man ijitama'a' (one who met) is better than the phrase 'man ra'ahu' (one who saw him) used by Ibn al-Hajib. The reason is that 'ra'ahu' (saw) would exclude someone like 'Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum, who was blind and thus could not literally 'see' the Prophet. The commentator then explains why length of companionship is not a condition for the Prophet's Companions, although it is required linguistically and customarily for others. The justification is that even a momentary meeting with the Prophet in faith confers an honor (sharaf) upon that person that no one else receives. This honor is so great that it elevates even the briefest companionship to a status that makes the person a Sahabi and grants him the inherent 'adalah.

Key Terms
صحابي
عدول
اجتماع
اجتمع
رآه
شرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A Sahabi must have spent a long time with the Prophet or narrated many hadiths.
Correction: The definition is broad: even a brief meeting suffices, and narration is not required.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator prefer the phrase 'man ijitama'a' over 'man ra'ahu' in defining a Sahabi?
A) Because 'ijitama'a' includes meeting in non-physical sense
B) Because 'ra'ahu' excludes blind Companions like 'Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum
C) Because 'ijitama'a' implies a longer companionship
D) Because 'ra'ahu' is not found in the Qur'an

Key Takeaway
A Sahabi is defined solely by meeting the Prophet in faith, even if briefly; this meeting confers a special honor that makes all Companions upright.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you honor all the Companions equally, or do you find yourself prioritizing those with more famous stories? Ask Allah to purify your heart from any bias against the less-known Companions like 'Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum.
?
If you were to meet the Prophet today in faith for even a single moment, what would you say? Are you living in a way that would make that meeting an honor for you?
?
The companion 'Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum was blind but still recognized as a Sahabi. Do you judge people's status in religion based on outward appearances or worldly achievements? Repent and align your heart with the sunnah.
